Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

Basic Understanding of the Sino-Japanese Problem (Part 1) 38

— Zhou Xianwen

— After reading Mr. Yamazaki Yasuzumi's "Anti-Japanese China" —

In September of this year, Mr. Yamazaki Yasuzumi, a famous Japanese economist, traveled to China and arrived in Shanghai via the Jinpu Railway from Beiping. I did not know Mr. Yamazaki originally, but one day I was introduced to him by a friend and had a brief meeting. At that time, he immediately expressed his hope to hear the opinions of Chinese economists in Shanghai who opposed Japan. He repeatedly stated that this trip was purely a personal action and had nothing to do with the Japanese authorities. He requested that the conversation be free and that we did not need to be polite to each other. Therefore, two days later, I introduced a certain gentleman who advocated "resistance against Japan to save the country" to meet him. Firstly, because they were talking very vigorously, I couldn't interrupt. Secondly, because I knew that I was just a scholar and even if I had opinions, I couldn't represent any party. Therefore, regarding the Sino-Japanese problem, I didn't express anything that day. The next day, Mr. Yamazaki left Shanghai for Beijing and then returned to his country.

Now, he sent me a magazine from Tokyo, which contains his great work. The title is printed in red ink and is called "Anti-Japanese China." The article is over ten thousand words long and describes his experiences, what he heard, and what he felt during this trip to China. According to him: the anti-Japanese sentiment in China is indeed better on the surface than in the past, but in essence, it is more profound than in the past. It has gone through "three stages" of development, and now it has turned from anti-Japanese sentiment of the Fascist front to anti-Japanese sentiment of the People's Front. He also said that he met many famous people from all walks of life in China. Among them were "China's Gorky" Mr. Lu Xun, "brave general of the anti-Japanese and national salvation movement" Mr. Zhang Naiqi, "senior Chinese educator" Mr. Huang Yanpei, and Mr. Pan Gongzhan. In addition, he also met Mr. Xu Xinliu, Mr. Fu Sinian, Mr. Ma Yinchu, Mr. Chu Fucheng, Mr. Xiao Tongzi, Mr. Cheng Cangbo, Mr. Luo Jialun, Mr. Hu Zhengzhi, and discussed the Sino-Japanese problem and heard their "high opinions."

However, the "high opinions" of these many famous people from all walks of life on the Sino-Japanese problem are obviously not very similar. He used a method of concealing their names, saying that "a certain gentleman" told him, "It is best for Japan to develop towards Southeast Asia and not attack China." This is like saying: since the robber has entered the door, please let him attack the neighbors next door. The Chinese, who claim that China is a country of etiquette, don't even know Confucius's clear instruction "do not do to others what you do not want done to yourself." No wonder Mr. Yamazaki wants to "conceal his name." In fact, "please develop towards Southeast Asia," why does "a certain gentleman" need to instruct this? Japanese imperialism has long listed Southeast Asia as one of its "development" targets, and it is already proceeding step by step. May I ask: what does Japanese imperialism really love about China? Why would it abandon the easy and attack the difficult, not "develop" in Southeast Asia, which is easier to obtain, but attack China, which has complicated relationships? Taking a step back, even if Japanese imperialism can accept the "certain gentleman"'s instruction and abandon China for Southeast Asia, saying that Japan can do without China after obtaining Southeast Asia is just a dream of those who do not understand the "nature of imperialist foreign expansion." What is certain is that "Mr. Fu Sinian of the Academia Sinica" told him that "Japan is indeed overpopulated, and China also suffers from overpopulation, and its resources are also very weak. Even if there are some resources, it is not easy to develop them." This is like saying: the robber has entered the door and is pleading bitterly. Although it is a bit more enlightened than the "using neighbors as a barrier" argument of a certain gentleman, it is also quite pitiful. Therefore, Mr. Yamazaki has the impression of "please don't set your sights on China, Japan." In fact, I once said at a Sino-Japanese problem symposium convened by the Shen Bao that the so-called "overpopulation" is just an excuse for Japan's foreign aggression. Japan's current foreign aggression is due to the overabundance of products rather than overpopulation. Looking back, Japan launched the September 18th Incident under the name of overpopulation and successively occupied the four northeastern provinces of China, but so far five years have passed, and the facts prove that very few Japanese have moved to the northeast. If we truly believe that Japan's foreign aggression is due to its need to address overpopulation, and also believe that China's overpopulation can truly be addressed through foreign aggression (please note this major premise), then no matter how bitterly Mr. Fu Sinian pleads and says that "China also suffers from overpopulation, and its resources are also very weak," I am afraid there is still no sufficient reason to reject Japan's aggression. The so-called "weakness" is originally the antonym of abundance, and is a relative term. If we have no way to prove that Japan's resources are indeed richer than China's, or that China's resources are indeed weaker than Japan's (at least that China's resources are as weak as Japan's), then China is still a target for Japanese aggression. Didn't Mr. Fu continue to say that China "even if there are some resources, it is not easy to develop them"? Good! China has some resources, but it is not easy to develop them. At the same time, all the resources that Japan has are almost developed, so Japan may as well come and help China develop these resources that are not easy to develop. The robber has entered the door, and if we say that our home is also very poor, and even if my wife has some gold jewelry in her hand, it is not easy to take it out, using these words to deal with the robber, apart from expressing a pitiful appearance, there is really no sufficient reason to refuse the robber's robbery. To be honest, China's resources are not few, at least not fewer than Japan's. But Japan definitely cannot invade China just because China has more resources. Moreover, Japan's so-called overpopulation is a "complete" lie.

Secondly, there is the opinion of "senior Chinese educator" Mr. Huang Yanpei, who told Mr. Yamazaki: "There is a saying in Shanghai called 'poisoning a tiger to death after eating arsenic.' If Japan, the tiger, really wants the lives of the Chinese people, then the Chinese people will eat the arsenic of communism and fight to the death together." Mr. Huang's opinion, which carries a bit of threat, is obviously "stronger" ten thousand times than the "using neighbors as a barrier" argument of a certain gentleman and the pleading argument of Mr. Fu. Because of this, Mr. Huang's relatively "tough" opinion has obviously aroused considerable attention from Mr. Yamazaki. Therefore, Mr. Yamazaki said: In China, "there is a pro-Russian consciousness hidden within the anti-Japanese consciousness. This is something Japan should consider most." Furthermore, he said: "Looking at the big picture, China's fate will either incline towards Japan or towards Soviet Russia. But at this time, it is not only a crisis for the Chinese government, but also a major crisis for Japan." And the final conclusion is: "If Japan does not first establish a theory and method on how to make China and Japan coexist and prosper in a fair and collaborative manner, then Japan will be in danger of being defeated by Soviet Russia." Of course, "poisoning a tiger to death after eating arsenic" is a passive measure of last resort. However, strictly speaking, these words still carry a threatening tone, and the real hope is still that Japan, the tiger, can "leave a way for the people." If we think that arsenic is a poison (premise), and the purpose of eating it is only to passively poison the tiger to death, then it is not necessary. It is better to use a little bit of strength to resist the tiger. What we want to strive for is not to poison the death of others with our own death, but how to escape from death. If unfortunately, we are also willing to use the last bit of strength to eat arsenic and fight the tiger to death.

Furthermore, there is the opinion of "brave general of the anti-Japanese and national salvation movement" Mr. Zhang Naiqi, who told Mr. Yamazaki, "Our proposal is only to resist Japan, not to exclude Japan." "What we want to fight against is Japanese imperialism or Japanese aggression, definitely not Japan or the Japanese people." With such a bright and upright declaration, Mr. Yamazaki of course expressed his approval, so he always said: "First: I have no objection to the Chinese people fighting against imperialism... but I am afraid that the Chinese government cannot fight imperialism thoroughly." "Second: China's anti-Japanese sentiment is of course hoped to succeed, but after success, how will it be built?" Most of the answers from Chinese celebrities to these two questions are "looking around and talking about other things." But these two questions are the central argument of Mr. Yamazaki's "Anti-Japanese China," and I will briefly discuss them as far as my limited knowledge allows. However, due to various reasons, I cannot speak my mind freely. Please readers "do not misinterpret the meaning due to the words."

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

How to Study Agricultural Disciplines (Part 1) 39

— Zhang Boyu, Professor of the College of Agriculture, Jinling University

(I) What is Called Agriculture?

People use labor to cultivate the land, adapting to the climate and terrain as appropriate and meeting local needs, to produce plants and animals for our use - selecting seeds, cultivating, protecting, managing, and distributing agricultural products are all agricultural activities. This comprehensive production technique based on land is collectively known as agriculture. We know that human emotions, perceptions, thoughts, or attitudes themselves cannot affect the growth of plants and animals. However, the formation of experience in agricultural technology is not only a technique but also knowledge combined from various causes and effects, and natural laws. This organized knowledge is agricultural science.

After reading the above, we can summarize by saying that agriculture is a cultivation and production enterprise that combines labor and land.

(II) What are the Characteristics of Agriculture?

Although agriculture is a production enterprise like industry and commerce, it has many unique limitations. Here, we will mention one or two of the most significant ones:

(1) Agriculture Depends on Land; Without Land, There is No Agriculture. The cultivation of all crops entirely requires land. Even animal husbandry and sericulture, on the surface, seem unrelated to land, but their feed, like pasture and mulberry leaves, grows on land. Furthermore, the fertility of the land and the allocation of land are directly related to agriculture. Therefore, land is one of the most essential elements of agricultural production.

(2) Agriculture Contains Regionality. The amount of rainfall, the temperature, the soil's composition and fertility, the slope and flatness of the terrain, the length of sunshine, and the climate's temperature all directly impact agricultural production. However, conditions vary from place to place, so agricultural organization also varies. The agriculture of area A may not be suitable for area B, European and American agriculture may not be suitable for China, and the agriculture of northern and southern China differs greatly.

(3) Agriculture Contains Seasonality. The germination, flowering, fruiting, and all management of agricultural plants must follow the changing seasons and cannot be shortened or advanced. Although some people are working to try to advance or extend the growing season, the effect is minimal and will not be universally adopted. Therefore, agricultural improvement will never be as rapid as in industry and commerce.

(III) Agricultural Vocational Education

Before discussing this issue, we must first understand what vocational education is. Education is an enterprise that aims to comprehensively solve life's problems. However, life's demands vary in different aspects and nature, so the methods of development also differ. Vocational education is essentially ordinary education, but after the division of labor, the knowledge and skills required for various occupations must be specialized. Only in the context of community life can there be occupations. Therefore, vocational education can be said to adapt to the needs of society, cultivate vocational talents with specialized skills, produce what others need through specialized activities, and indirectly seek one's own needs. As for what agricultural vocational education is, it uses specialized methods or techniques to maintain or produce the growth of plants and animals, directly providing raw materials for society, and indirectly seeking a fulfilling life for agricultural producers. Therefore, all education related to agriculture, such as farming, sericulture, forestry, animal husbandry, aquaculture, horticulture, agricultural product manufacturing, and rural cooperation, is called agricultural education. Therefore, we know that there are many occupations in society, and the nature of each occupation is different. Therefore, vocational education must also be classified according to the nature of the occupation. Agricultural vocational education is one type of vocational education, but the training of students focuses entirely on agricultural disciplines and skills.

(IV) The Purpose and Scope of Agricultural Education

This point can be discussed from three aspects:

(1) The Purpose and Scope of Elementary School Agricultural Education. The purpose of elementary school agricultural education is not to cultivate a good farmer but to enable children to have a correct and broad understanding of the natural environment and the relationship between nature and humans. At the same time, it aims to generate children's interest in agriculture and foster sympathy and respect for farmers' lives and work. At the very least, it should enable children to have a considerable understanding of subjects such as plants and livestock, which is a basic preparation for entering secondary agricultural schools in the future. Therefore, the implementation of elementary school agricultural education, in addition to more observation and practice, should also include both successful and failed practices, with mutual comparisons, as the basis for clear and experimental teaching.

(2) The Purpose and Scope of Agricultural Colleges. Agricultural colleges are the highest academic institutions for agricultural research. They should conduct in-depth research on various agricultural issues. Therefore, they should conduct in-depth research on surveying agriculture, studying agricultural sciences, and the fundamental issues of agricultural management. At the same time, they must also focus on experimentation and design, as well as the study of agricultural theory.

(3) The Purpose and Scope of Secondary Agricultural Schools. Secondary agricultural schools are intermediate between agricultural colleges and elementary schools, so their purpose is naturally different from the above two. According to the regulations of the Ministry of Education: "The purpose of secondary agricultural schools is to cultivate talents capable of independently managing various agricultural activities; farm technicians; agricultural instructors; personnel for agricultural cooperation, agricultural extension, rural improvement, and elementary school agriculture teachers." Therefore, secondary agricultural students must not only have a deep understanding and proficiency in the skills of various practical agricultural operations but also have a deep understanding of various undertakings in rural society. Their mental agility and physical health must be noted. These are the foundation and preparation for future service or further education.

(V) What Kind of Agricultural Vocational Education Do We Need?

The establishment of modern agricultural education in China dates back to the 22nd year of Guangxu. Although the education system has undergone many changes and the school names have been changed many times, the importance of agricultural education has not diminished. However, although agricultural schools have been increasing year by year, agricultural school graduates have no way out, and our country's agriculture has not made any progress. Is this because modern agricultural education is not suitable for the needs of our society, or is there no need to conduct agricultural education? Regarding this point, we must thoroughly understand the factors that led to the failure of agricultural education in the past. Mr. Zhang Zhiwen, an agricultural education expert, said: "The failure of agricultural education in the past was mainly due to the perfunctory and careless teaching. Students have not received practical training, so they have no ability to engage in specialized occupations. To fulfill its mission, secondary agricultural schools should first determine the specific guidelines for implementing agricultural education." Mr. Zhang is one of the few agricultural education experts in the country and has been engaged in agricultural education for many years, so he naturally has a unique perspective on this point. Therefore, he also has the following views on the implementation of agricultural education in China in the future: A. Secondary schools in each rural area of the province should solve their specialized problems according to local needs. B. The curriculum should be adapted to the needs of the local area. C. The number of students enrolled should be based on the number of agricultural talents needed in the school district. D. The talents cultivated should be allocated in a comprehensive manner. E. Survey the employment status of graduates as a basis for school improvement. F. Conduct supplementary education for out-of-school youth in the school district. In addition, the content of the school should be as substantial as possible, the farms should be as large as possible, the books should be as rich as possible, and the teachers must have both knowledge and ability. If those who run agricultural education in the future can truly follow Mr. Zhang's words and do it conscientiously, then I can say that the agricultural school graduates in the future will not have no way out, and the agriculture taught in the school will not be unable to establish a close relationship with society. In short, agricultural education in the future must be integrated with society, and students must have rich knowledge and experience, and be able to practice in the field. Only in this way can China's agricultural education fulfill its mission and embark on the road of agricultural revitalization.

(VI) Why Study Agriculture?

Regarding the purpose and scope of establishing agricultural departments in schools at all levels, we have discussed it roughly above. We will further discuss why modern secondary school students should study agriculture. This point can be discussed from several aspects:

(1) Agriculture Itself. Agriculture is a basic industry. Whether it is people's clothing, food, housing, transportation, all kinds of raw materials are directly and indirectly derived from agricultural products. Even if we want to revitalize industry, we have to improve agriculture. Because most of the raw materials in industry are taken from agricultural products. According to Professor Bu Kai of Jinling University, the total cultivated area in China is 1,578,000,000 mu. At least 350 million people directly depend on the land for their livelihoods, and more than 100 million people indirectly depend on the land to maintain their livelihoods. Therefore, dividing the land by the total population, each person gets only three mu of land. Moreover, our natural population growth rate is very high. According to a survey by the Department of Agricultural Economics of Jinling University, it is 1.43%. If we estimate the total population of the country as 450 million, then the total population of the country will increase by 6.4 million people within a year. We see such population pressure, and we can only solve it by improving agriculture. Furthermore, we have been using the land for more than 4,000 years, and the fertility of the land has been almost exhausted. If we do not engage in active cultivation, it is really difficult to maintain it. Therefore, we should study agriculture so that agricultural technology progresses day by day, farmers' knowledge increases day by day, people become richer day by day, and the country becomes stronger day by day. Then, we can compete with the world's powers and not be subjected to economic oppression.

Current Commentary

Sino-British Continued Survey of the Yunnan-Burma Border 40

— Li

The issue of surveying the undetermined section of the Sino-British Yunnan-Burma border has been delayed for forty years since 1897. Only on April 9th of last year did our government reach an agreement with Britain to form a border survey committee composed of two commissioners each from China and Britain, and one neutral commissioner appointed by the League of Nations, with the neutral commissioner as the chairman. The committee went to the undetermined section of the Yunnan-Burma border to conduct a joint survey. The committee was established in July, and on December 1st, our commissioners Liang Yugao and Yi Mingde, British commissioners Colegrave and Glass, and the neutral commissioner, Swiss national Islam, arrived at Huthsan to begin the survey. By April of this year, the work was suspended due to the arrival of the rainy season and the prevalence of miasma. Our commissioner Liang Yugao returned to Beijing to report. Now that the rainy season has passed, Commissioner Liang has set off again for Yunnan, intending to continue the survey from New Year's Day next year, and complete the entire survey before the rainy season. The long-pending border issue may be partially resolved as a result.

According to Article 3 of the Sino-British Burma Convention of 1886, "The Sino-Burmese border shall be jointly surveyed and demarcated by commissioners appointed by the two governments." Subsequently, China and Britain repeatedly sent high-ranking officials to survey and demarcate the boundary line. In 1894, our country and Britain concluded the Yunnan-Burma Border and Commerce Convention, consisting of twenty articles. In 1897, another Yunnan-Burma Border and Commerce Convention with nineteen supplementary articles was concluded with Britain. At that time, the survey personnel, ignorant of geography, mistakenly included the area outside the Hanlong, Tianma, Huju, and Tiebi Four Passes entirely into Burmese territory. In 1897, China and Britain again sent commissioners to survey the Yunnan-Burma border. What was surveyed at that time was the section starting from the northern tip of Gaoshan in Tengchong County, extending south and east to the Nam Pan River, a tributary of the Nam Ting River, in Zhenkang County. The areas north of the northern tip of Gaoshan, such as Pianma and Jiangxinpo, were not demarcated due to disputes between China and Britain. This is the undetermined northern section. As for the section from the Nam Ting River south to the Nam Ma River, a tributary of the Nam Ka River, in Lancang County, including the mineral-rich Ban Hong and Ximeng areas, the Qing government, according to the provisions of the Supplementary Articles to the Yunnan-Burma Border and Commerce Convention, sent Liu Wansheng and Chen Can in 1899, following the map line presented by Minister to Britain Xue Fucheng, to conduct a joint survey with British representative Scott. The boundary line proposed by the Xue map starts from the Nam Ting River, goes south along the mountain ridge, and follows Gongming Mountain to the place where the Nam Ma River flows into the Nam Ka River, placing the upper, middle, and lower Hulumu tribes of Ban Hong under the jurisdiction of Yunnan Province, and the areas belonging to Ban Zhu under the jurisdiction of Burma. At that time, Scott insisted that the latitude and longitude recorded in Xue's map and documents did not match, and produced another map, firmly insisting that the line should start from the Nam Ting River, go south and turn east, follow Kongming Mountain (an allusion to Gongming Mountain), and go to the Nam Ka River, placing Ban Hong and other places under the jurisdiction of Burma. The two sides argued endlessly and failed to demarcate the line. This is the undetermined southern section. What the current Sino-British Yunnan-Burma Border Survey Committee is surveying is this section of the boundary line.

The task of the Sino-British Yunnan-Burma Border Survey Committee is said to be to conduct on-the-ground surveys of geographical, political, and historical factors to determine the true meaning of the text of the Supplementary Articles to the Yunnan-Burma Border and Commerce Convention of 1897 as a reference for future demarcation. Political and historical factors are part of human geography and can indeed serve as important references for demarcation. However, we know that since 1897, the British have created many "faits accomplis" in the undetermined area. For example, in the Lancang area, the British have established more than 200 churches. Wherever churches are established, they form a special area that is not under the jurisdiction of our country. These situations increase the difficulty of demarcation. Therefore, we hope that the survey commissioners will strictly limit their research on political and historical factors to the facts before 1897; otherwise, this survey may still be delayed.

Shangdu Dispatch: Since the bandit-puppet troops invading Hongge'ertu began their attack on the 11th of this month, up to the 19th, they have engaged in numerous battles, large and small, with the Sui troops, but have not succeeded in their aims. Recent Political Situation in Guizhou Province; Setting Principles for Banning Opium, Implementing Military Industry, and Building Roads 65

Guilin Dispatch: Since the provincial government of Guizhou Province moved to Guilin, the environment has changed, and all administrative steps and major plans for the current situation urgently need to be properly discussed. Therefore, a joint conference of the Guizhou Provincial Party, government, and military was specially convened in Guilin on the 10th of the month. In addition to Li Zongren, Bai Chongxi, Huang Xuchu, and others, senior military and government officials all attended. The internal Party, government, and military issues of Guizhou Province, the future proposals of Guizhou Province for the current situation, and the contributions to the central government were all discussed. On the 12th, President Sun Ke flew to Guilin, and Li, Bai, and others were busy receiving him. The meeting was suspended for several days. Taking advantage of Sun's visit to Guizhou, the Guizhou authorities specially asked Sun to submit various proposals from Guizhou Province to the central government on behalf of the province. The joint conference on internal affairs in Guizhou Province also had many resolutions. In terms of politics, the focus was on developing agriculture, forestry, and mining, strictly enforcing the prohibition of opium and gambling, and setting nine principles for the prohibition of smoking: (1) Before the implementation of the ban, a large-scale official announcement will be held. (2) Conduct a registration of smokers. (3) People in this province are strictly prohibited from eating opium. Those who are already addicted to opium and are under 45 years old will be ordered to quit within three months. (4) Opium paste is exclusively sold. (5) Opium paste is exclusively sold. (6) Confiscate and destroy opium paraphernalia. (7) Opium cessation drugs are manufactured and sold by the Wuzhou Pharmaceutical Factory. (8) Criminal punishment is handled in accordance with the Central Government's Provisional Regulations on the Punishment of Opium Prohibition Crimes. Regarding finance and banking, since the ratio between Guizhou currency and national currency was determined to be plus six, as of the 1st of this month, all provincial revenues and expenditures are based on national currency. Except for defense costs, all tax collection agencies still collect in haoquan converted into national currency, and expenditures are paid at 80% of the national currency amount. The silver dollar notes originally issued by the Guizhou Provincial Treasury are fully recovered by the Guangxi Bank at a price of $1.30. Before they are recovered, they are still used as $1.30. Bai Chongxi is still working hard to reorganize the troops and run military reclamation areas, etc., and has not been able to go north for a while. In addition to those who were dismissed and transferred to military reclamation areas for cultivation, a portion of the active soldiers in the Guangxi army were transferred to build roads. The Guiwu Highway is a construction project that Guangxi is eager to carry out after the relocation of the government. The route has been surveyed by personnel, and construction is currently underway, with soldiers from the 19th Division, 21st Division, and 24th Division responsible for different sections. The troops of the 19th Division had already arrived at Chencun Tang Station on the 16th, and the 24th Division also began work according to the designated section. As for Party affairs, they are still proceeding as before, and there is no clear order for reorganization. According to the Guizhou authorities, there is no need to rush to reorganize Party affairs in Guizhou Province, because Party affairs in Guizhou have always been handled in a unified and coordinated manner, without any disputes, and the organization is sound, so it is not appropriate to reorganize it rashly. Therefore, Party affairs in Guangxi are still handled as before, maintaining the status quo, and the reorganization is still under consideration. After the closing of the joint conference of the Party, government, and military, senior officials have returned separately, and in the future, they will implement the decisions of the joint conference, and the situation in Guangxi will show a new look. (November 18)

Suzhou: Assigning Personnel to Persuade Tenant Farmers to Pay Rent 66

County Magistrate Deng Xianghai, in view of the fact that it has been more than ten days since the various industry stores opened warehouses to collect rent, but there has been no improvement, and the total amount has not reached 20%. He is certain that the tenant farmers in Chefang, Xiangcheng, Yinshan, and other villages resisted the rent last year as a group due to the famine, and this year they are still delaying going to the stores to pay the rent. In addition to issuing a public notice, limiting the tenant farmers in each village to complete the rent payment within twenty days, and implementing detention without leniency, on the 22nd, Zhao Jintang, Zhang Yixin, and Jiang Yunjie were also assigned to Chefang and other villages to convene village chiefs and headmen to give speeches, persuade, and notify the tenant farmers to quickly go to the stores to pay the rent.

County Government Planning to Establish District Granaries 67

The county government, under orders, is planning to establish district granaries to store grain for famine preparedness. It immediately ordered the various district offices to find suitable locations for the district granaries. They have successively reported back to the county government on the selected locations. However, the grain storage in the district granaries should be undertaken by the landlords, so the county government will discuss the grain storage issue with the landlords in the next few days.

Wuxi: Station Master of the Train Station Suspended from Duty 68

Li Guisheng, the former station master of the train station in this county, and others, were previously suspected of being involved in smuggling incidents at the station. The two railway bureaus suspended him from duty and immediately transferred Yu Shucheng, the deputy station master of Suzhou, and Sun Chaodong, the station master of Kunshan, to Wuxi to take over. They have been in office for nearly half a year. Last month, Yu and Sun were secretly accused to the railway bureau of privately collecting illegal fees, colluding with each other, and damaging the reputation of the railway. The bureau immediately ordered Section Chief Wang of the Transportation Section to come to Wuxi to investigate thoroughly. He investigated with a certain bank, but did not get any reliable information. After a thorough investigation, he finally found some clues and first suspended Gu Jiaxiang, a low-ranking clerk in the station master's office. Yesterday, the railway bureau also ordered Yu Shucheng and Sun Chaodong to be suspended from duty. Wang Jisheng was appointed to fill Yu's vacancy, Feng Xiqing was appointed to fill Wang's vacancy, and Yang Qisun was temporarily appointed to fill Sun's vacancy.

Supervising Various Silk and Yarn Factories 69

In order to understand the equipment of factories in various counties, the Ministry of Industry sent factory inspector Liu Bingheng to Wuxi to inspect. At the same time, the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department also sent factory inspector Cheng Qiyuan to Wuxi to join Liu Bingheng in the inspection. Yesterday, the Wuxi County Construction Bureau sent factory inspector Chang Wang Youfang to accompany them to inspect the factories that meet the requirements of the Factory Law ("workers numbering over thirty people"). At 9:00 AM on the 22nd, they continued to go to various silk and yarn factories for inspection.

Comforting Soldiers in Suiyuan 70

Because all circles in this county enthusiastically contributed to comfort the soldiers fighting the enemy in Suiyuan with one day's earnings, County Magistrate Long Tiyao also initiated and advocated this, and decided to comfort the frontline soldiers with all of his personal earnings for one day. It is heard that Secretary Zai Rongsan, Section Chief Li Shouhuan of the First Section, Section Chief Huang Fu of the Second Section, and Section Chief Xu Yingtu of the Third Section also participated. The other county government officials are also willing to donate to contribute. In addition, the students and all the teachers and staff of the county middle school specially launched a ten-day campaign to reduce food and eat vegetarian meals, and remit the remaining expenses to the front lines to provide comfort.

Changshu: Yangfu Road to Open Next Month 71

In order to develop transportation along the river and cultivate the prosperity of the Xihu Road, the Jiangsu Provincial Construction Department specially expanded northward from Yangjian Station on the western section of the Xihu Road to build the Yangfu Road. The road is thirty kilometers long with six bridges. Construction began in the spring of this year, and the entire road has now been completed. It is learned that the right to operate the road will still be undertaken by the Xihu Long-Distance Bus Company. Manager Wang Xiaolai has negotiated a contract with the Construction Department, which is generally in place. The company is now building station houses along the way and plans to set up two stations in Gangtou Dahe. In addition, it is decided to set up agency stations first, and then add more as the business develops in the future. It is heard that the road is scheduled to officially open on December 15th.

Business and Education Circles Launch Campaign to Comfort Sui 72

Because bandit-puppet troops invaded our Sui territory, Chairman Fu led troops to fight fiercely. The Education Association and the County Chamber of Commerce held a temporary meeting on the afternoon of the 20th to organize a Suiyuan Bandit Suppression Support Association. They immediately sent an urgent telegram to Chairman Fu and the various soldiers to comfort and encourage them, and launched a one-day campaign to enthusiastically donate for use on the front lines. The office has been set up in the County Chamber of Commerce.

Major Theft Case at the Bank of Communications 73

A major theft case suddenly occurred at the Bank of Communications here the day before yesterday. The amount lost has been determined in the two iron boxes in the office, but the amount in the vault has not been checked yet because the manager went to Shanghai. All employees and service staff are under strict surveillance. The Changshu branch of the Bank of Communications was established earliest, so there are many deposits. Last year, it built a new house on Daonan Street, facing the Bank of China, and its business became more developed. Recently, Manager Zhang Guliu asked for leave to go to Shanghai for his daughter's wedding. On the morning of the 21st, all the employees were working in the office when they suddenly discovered that the two iron boxes were damaged. After opening them, the stocks, more than 10,000 yuan in cash, and the gold and jewelry sent by the manager's wife were completely lost. The business was suspended, and the case was reported to the Public Security Bureau. Chief Chen Yuchu of the bureau, considering the seriousness of the case, immediately went to investigate with the detective team leader. The iron boxes were pried open with a steel drill. The doors of the vault also had similar damage. However, the amount of the loss is difficult to know for sure before Manager Zhang returns to Changshu for inventory. In short, there were no signs of opening or closing at any of the doors, so it seems there is no doubt that it was done by an insider. Subsequently, the Public Security Bureau summoned all the employees of the bank, large and small, for questioning. As a result, only a temporary cook named Li San, who had been working for only two days, was highly suspected and temporarily detained in the bureau. That night, none of the employees were allowed to return home, and the detectives were keeping a close watch on the bank. A telegram has been sent to the manager in Shanghai to report the matter, and he is expected to return to Changshu today to handle the matter.

Eight Rural Women Drowned in Capsized Boat 74

On the 21st, there was a customary incense pilgrimage at the Xiaxi Lane of Meilitang Bridge. Dozens of incense boats went there to offer incense. A boat named Xiaxing, carrying more than fifty rural women, capsized near the Dahong Bridge because it was carrying too many passengers. By accident, the side of the boat hit the bridge pier, causing the boat to capsize. More than fifty rural women fell into the water. Cries and screams filled the air, and there was great chaos. The nearby farmers rushed to the rescue and saved most of them, but eight elderly women drowned. Their bodies were not recovered until late at night. Afterwards, the Public Security Bureau arrested Xia Xing, the owner of the boat and the leader of the incense pilgrimage. It is heard that most of the dead rural women were from Guli Village. After the county government reported the matter on the 22nd, it ordered the families to collect the bodies.

Wujiang: Organizing a Comforting Committee 75

Yesterday, people from all walks of life in this county convened a meeting at the county government to establish a committee to comfort the Suiyuan bandit suppression soldiers. County Magistrate Xu chaired the meeting: (1) It was resolved to set up a committee of seventeen people, with each from the county party and others to be committee members, and decided to appoint the 216th regiment, the county government, the county party, the county chamber of commerce, and the provincial rural teachers as standing committee members; (2) It was resolved that all districts should organize comforting branch associations, and the district offices should immediately convene all sectors to organize with the various branches.

Zhenjiang: Reorganizing the Zhensu Section of the Grand Canal 76

The Jiangsu Provincial Grand Canal, south of the Yangtze River, is extremely important in terms of water conservancy and transportation. The provincial government previously determined the Zhensu section navigation plan in accordance with the Grand Canal reorganization discussion and survey, and prepared an engineering budget. In addition to implementing the dredging of the Zhenjiang Dantu to Wuxi Luoshe section within the scope of the drought relief project in the 23rd year, the remaining unfinished dredging project in the 24th year and the construction of the water gate engineering along the Yangtze River should be continued. The ship locks, culverts, diversion rivers, and dredging works from Wujin through Shitangwan to Wujiang were all estimated to cost 2 million yuan. Because the provincial government asked the National Economic Committee to allocate funds to assist in handling, but because of the large amount of funds required, it was feared that it would be difficult to prepare, and it was determined to set another 25-year project plan, and first implement the dredging of the Dantu to Zhenjiang section, and build a control water gate, estimating that the project cost will need more than 260,000 yuan, and also requested the Economic Committee to check and allocate 180,000 yuan to facilitate the process. Soon the reply was approved, and it was agreed to assist with 100,000 yuan. Recently, the provincial government has compiled a project budget, and ordered the Jiangnan Water Conservancy Engineering Office to rush to start construction.

Jiangyin: Ballon Lands on Sand Islet 77

A balloon landed on the sky over the Shanzheng Bridge in Shazhou the day before yesterday. When landing, the height was 40 inches and the width was more than 20 inches. The instrument inside the ball has not been damaged. It was picked up by the soldiers of the second squad of the 11th Security Brigade. The ball also stated that it was the Central Observatory's test balloon. Those who picked it up when it fell and did not damage it would be rewarded with 20 yuan in legal tender. If the instrument was slightly damaged, the reward would be 15 yuan in legal tender. The squad soldiers sent the balloon to the brigade headquarters on the 20th and sent a letter to the Central Observatory to collect it in Cheng.

Danyang: County Chamber of Commerce Selects Standing Committee 78

The County Chamber of Commerce of this county held its first executive committee meeting yesterday. Eleven members attended, and Jiang Kesheng was publicly elected as chairman. Many important cases were discussed. The standing committee members were then elected by ballot. As a result, Jiang Kesheng, Jiang Jingtao, Hu Yinjie, He Leixia, and Zhan Shuofu were elected as standing committee members. According to law, the chairman was elected among the standing committee members. As a result of the election, Hu Yinjie was elected as chairman.

Haizhou: Huimin Sluice Gate Fully Completed 79

The Huimin Sluice Gate at Zhangjiakou in the fourth district of Shuyang County started construction last month and has now been fully completed on the 16th of this month. The river embankment is now being repaired to speed up the process and can be completed in one week. A water release ceremony will be held on a selected date. It is verified that the total cost of the sluice gate is 4,000 yuan. The sluice gate design adopts a new style. Once the water is released, the water volume in the area can be adjusted accordingly.

Jiashan: Detailed Report on Jiashan Land Survey 81

Since the establishment of the Jiashan Land Survey Office, the various businesses have been divided into seven groups: surveying, checking for integration, map making, list making, proofreading, and investigation. All the surveyed land has a public bulletin board, and the public bulletin board members are stationed in the office to post. After the announcement, the business owners take the deed grain string and documentary evidence to the office to check the map book. Expired time will be the final decision. From May 1st to November 5th of this year, five counties have been completed, but the business owners do not understand the pros and cons, and most of them are waiting and watching, or entrusting tenants to report on their behalf. There are few recognitions and approvals. As a result, the deadline has been extended again and again, and notice slips have been issued to large households. Moreover, disputes have arisen due to property rights. In Xitang alone, there have been 32 disputes. The county government has specially formulated mediation measures and submitted them to the county government meeting for approval. Fair gentry are hired in various townships to organize land mediation committees. It will be organized in Xitang first. Those who have disputes can fill in an application form and apply for mediation. Another appraiser is hired to be stationed in the county government to make the final decision.

Cixi: Discovery of Undisclosed Military Bronze Seal 82

A resident named Shen, near Miaoshan Bridge in Cixi, recently passed through the Daibao Mountain foothills and saw a shepherd boy playing with something. Upon closer inspection, it was an ancient small bronze seal with a wide border, a yang style, and seal script that read, "Subject Seal Zhu Gui." The knife technique was elegant and simple. The back button was a crouching tiger with exquisite carving. Shen knew that this seal was a relic of General Zhu who fought bloodily against Bao Feng and fought against the enemy alone. He exchanged it for one yuan in legal tender. In order to preserve the historical celebrities and hero's handwriting, Shen plans to send it to the public education agency for display so that the public can pay their respects.

Hangzhou: Chrysanthemum Exhibition to Comfort Sui 83

Students of the Agricultural College of Zhejiang University, in view of the fact that the soldiers of Suiyuan are fighting for the country and the nation in the ice and snow, are eager to provide spiritual and material assistance, so they launched a chrysanthemum exhibition to comfort Sui. The exhibition was held at the Provincial People's Education Center on the lakeside for three days. With the approval of the school authorities, more than 1,600 kinds of precious chrysanthemums cultivated by the Horticultural Department of the college were displayed for people to visit and sell at a price, and all the proceeds were donated to the frontline soldiers of Suiyuan. Visitors were very enthusiastic. The meeting closed on the evening of the 22nd, with a total income of more than 200 yuan, which was remitted to the front.

Ningbo: Capture of Kidnappers at Sanbao Bridge 84

In the Du Guo area of Ci Dong Wenxi, a resident named Shen Wenjian, who runs a money shop in Shanghai and is quite wealthy, attracted the attention of bandits. On the morning of the 20th of this month, at 2 a.m., ten bandits, each wielding a weapon, planned to kidnap his daughter and demand a large ransom. Unexpectedly, they mistakenly entered the home of Shen's neighbor, Zhou Deliu, and kidnapped Zhou's daughter, Fangqin (18 years old). Near the Xijing Hall, the bandits realized their mistake through the eyes of someone, so they decided to continue with the plan and took Zhou's daughter on a small boat pre-docked in the river, sailing towards Ningbo. When they arrived at the Sanbao Bridge on the Jiangbei shore of this port, they were intercepted by Zhou Caiyou, the seventh Baochang of Du Guo, who had been tracking them, and detectives who had come to Ningbo. Because it was still dark at the time, only two bandits were captured besides the hostage, while the others escaped. The hostage and the captured bandits were sent together to the Cixi County government for disposition.

Dredging the West Lake Waterway 85

The Ningxian City River Dredging Committee, recognizing that the water in the West Lake River is polluted and affects drinking water, plans to dredge the curved sections of the lake river and areas with poor water flow. Starting from Ma Yan Pond, they will open an outflow channel to connect to the city river to facilitate water flow, so that pollution does not accumulate and the water can be clarified. In addition, the section of the river from Ao Hua He Tou to 128 Bridge is narrow and winding, making it inconvenient for boats to travel back and forth. It is proposed to fill it in and build city houses.

Shaoxing: Organizing a Rear Support Association for Resistance Against the Enemy 86

The educational circles of Shaoxing, recognizing the seriousness of the national crisis and the urgency of defending the border, specially convened representatives from various schools on the afternoon of the 17th to discuss aid measures. It was decided to organize the Shaoxing Educational Circles Rear Support Association for Resistance Against the Enemy, and a founding meeting was held on the 19th at the Shiyong Education Association to engage in rear support work. This is intended to comfort the armed comrades at the front lines, who are resisting the enemy in cold weather with thin clothing, and to awaken the masses in the rear to prepare for extraordinary times.

Bengbu: Various Sectors Enthusiastically Donate to Aid the Border 87

People from all walks of life in Bengbu believe that since the bandits and puppets have invaded the border, they should enthusiastically donate to aid the soldiers guarding the territory. Members of the Chamber of Commerce first donated one day's salary to comfort the soldiers defending the border. In recent days, employees of stores, hospitals, schools, newspapers, cinemas, the New Transport Association, the People's Education Center, and private individuals have also risen up to raise funds to aid the border. Furthermore, students of Jianghuai Middle School implemented a suspension of cooking and fasting on the 19th, drinking only three portions of salt water each to use the day's meal expenses to aid the border and national defense construction. The Chamber of Commerce also convened representatives of various trade associations at 2 p.m. on the 19th to discuss one-day activity measures. Various industries enthusiastically donated, and once enough funds are collected, they will be remitted separately.

Donghua in a Difficult Battle: 3-3 Draw with La克斯 (Lakes) / Li Ning Absent Due to Illness, Guarding Strength Reduced / La克斯 (Lakes) Fights with Ten Men, Maintaining Advantage Throughout / Tense Performance by Both Sides, a Grand Spectacle 89

In this season's league, Donghua encountered a formidable opponent for the first time yesterday, La克斯 (Lakes), which is generally recognized as the bravest and most skilled team of this year. A Tense and Delightful Situation

Dai Linjing arrived soon after and kicked the ball into the goal, but it was disallowed because Wen Kui was offside. Soon after, Xu suffered a slight injury and left the field. He immediately re-entered after a moment and continued to press, eventually allowing Xu Wen Kui to shoot into the enemy's goal, creating a 3-3 draw. Donghua narrowly escaped defeat. They then tried to win, desperately struggling, and the entire army surrounded the enemy's goal. The inner guards also came out to assist, with a fierce aura. The enemy was besieged on all sides, and the atmosphere became more tense. La克斯 (Lakes) was flustered and unable to parry, showing signs of panic, and finally managed to hold on to their territory. They then quickly rushed into Donghua's territory. Bo Lin Gai was in a threatening posture, but ultimately failed. The game ended in a draw.

Educational News

Lecture by Visiting Professors Between China and England: Lecturer Zhang Pengchun Returns to China, Gives a Speech at the YMCA in Eight Immortals Bridge Yesterday, Entitled "Comparison of Chinese and English University Education" 99

For the purpose of promoting cultural exchange between China and England, a program for exchanging university lecturers was established. Last year, the Chinese professors who went to England included Li Shiyun, and the British professor who came to China was Evans. This year, the Chinese professor who went to England was Zhang Pengchun. Zhang is the younger brother of Zhang Boling, currently a professor at Nankai University and a lecturer at the University of Chicago in the United States. This time, he returned to China and came to Shanghai. At 3:00 PM yesterday, he gave a speech at the auditorium of the YMCA in Eight Immortals Bridge titled "A Comparison of British University Education and Chinese University Education." Since England has sixteen universities, and Mr. Zhang has already visited twelve, he has a deep understanding of British university education. The following is an excerpt of his speech, provided as a reference for those in China who are managing university education.

Historical Background of British Universities

Mr. Zhang first discussed the historical background of British universities, which can be divided into three periods. The first period universities, namely Oxford and Cambridge, have a history of six or seven hundred years and are the oldest universities in England, with a landowning background. The second period university is the University of London, established a hundred years ago, representing emerging industrial and commercial capitalists. The third period universities are the higher vocational schools in major cities forty years ago, focusing on new sciences, such as Manchester, Liverpool, and Leeds. However, even the old universities have now shifted to new trends.

Status of Universities in Society

British society is relatively stable and the pace of change is slower. Therefore, people in universities do not feel an immediate political responsibility, but their interest in studying politics is very strong, much stronger than in China. This strong interest is sufficient to encourage various political studies and discussions. Each faction has small groups, and even those with differing political views discuss openly, unlike Chinese university students whose interest in politics is too weak and too simplistic.

University Lifestyle

Generally, British university students' lifestyle is divided into small groups. Within each small group, teachers and students live together. This is because British universities are organized like religious monasteries. However, this atmosphere is now less prevalent, but communal living still exists. Their colleges are not based on academic departments but on residence. Those who live together form a college, providing multifaceted training, including character development, organizational skills, and the ability to handle social situations, teaching them how to be a person. They especially emphasize physical exercise, which is not just for a few but is required for everyone. Therefore, their collective living is particularly good.

Teaching Methods - The Tutorial System

Chinese universities mostly imitate the United States in their teaching methods, using lectures and a credit system, which has now aroused general dissatisfaction. England uses the tutorial system. When a student enters, they do not enter the entire university but first enter a college. They meet with a tutor at least once or twice a week, submit an essay for each meeting, and can freely talk with the tutor, allowing the tutor to understand the student's personality. However, sufficient funding is necessary because a tutor teaches a maximum of ten to twenty students per week. Moreover, the academic terms in England are different from those in China, with three terms per year, each lasting eight weeks. At the beginning of the term, they focus on stimulating the students' spirit and thinking, and they read and accumulate knowledge during the holidays, making it difficult to implement in China.

Requirements for Reforming University Education

How should Chinese university education be reformed? There are three fundamental conditions: (1) It is hoped that social order will become more organized day by day so that university education can be improved; (2) the cultivation of teachers; (3) creating a new educational atmosphere of human relationships, etc.

YMCA Held Map Drawing and Silent Mapping Competition Yesterday, with Over Two Hundred Participants, Mostly Students, and Groups Participating, Going to Various Schools to Hold Competitions 101

To encourage young people to become familiar with the geography of their country, the Shanghai YMCA specially held a map drawing and silent mapping competition. The silent mapping competition was held at the YMCA on Sichuan Road at 9:00 AM yesterday. The details are as follows:

Competition Details

The YMCA competition was divided into drawing and silent mapping. For the drawing competition, participants pre-registered and received drawing paper to complete their drawings, which were submitted yesterday. It is now said that more than 50 yuan has been accumulated. After the voluntary donations from the people of the sub-districts have been collected, and a whole number is formed, it will be remitted to the front line. The Shanghai Performing Arts Association, for the purpose of assisting the soldiers defending the territory of Suiyuan, convened a general meeting of representatives of its affiliated groups yesterday. A total of Hu Hensheng, Qian Wuliang, Li Junpan, Liu Ziyun, Shu Xiangjun, Zhou Tingkang, Wang Shaofeng, Zhang Shuqin, Ding Shoutang, Pei Yanghua, Li Xie-tang, Li Zhuan, Gai Nanxuanzhu Guo Shaomei, Ling Youxiang Jiang Xiaoxiao, Liu Chunshan, Lu Qiqi, Cheng Xiaoting, Wang Xiaoxin, Xiao Wenbin, Shi Chunxuan, Jiang Chunshen, Zhuang Haiquan, Zhu Guoliang, He Guisun, Zai Youyou, Chen Dabei, Gu Jianqiu, Wang Lianghong, Yu Yupin, Li Changjian, Xu Zheshen, Ye Yihua, Tang Bihua, Wang Manqing, Shen Xiaomei, Ding Xiaofang, Jin Xuefang and other more than forty people from Runyu Society, Pinghua Tanci Research Association, Comedian One-Man Show Research Association, Shanghai Opera Research Association, Suzhou Tan Opera Research Association, Drama Research Association, Yongyu Society, Shanghai Storytelling Research Association, Improved Ningbo Opera Research Association, Story Broadcasting Research Association, Huaiyang Pinghua Research Association, Weiyang Opera Research Association, Shaoxing Opera Research Association and other groups attended. The chairman first reported on the purpose of convening the meeting, and then resolved to organize the Shanghai Performing Arts Circle to initiate a support association for Suiyuan anti-Japanese soldiers, and resolved the assistance measures: (1) Organize the Shanghai Performing Arts Circle Suiyuan Anti-Japanese Soldiers Support Association. (4) All comrades, whether on the radio or in the venues, should do their best to publicize the anti-Japanese situation of the Suiyuan soldiers to the audience, in order to awaken compatriots across the country, rise up together, and share the heavy responsibility of saving the country, and enthusiastically donate money to provide rear support. (5) Regularly broadcast special programs to solicit donations from all walks of life.

National Product Factory Alliance

The China National Product Factory Alliance in this city yesterday issued a notice to member manufacturers stating that the invasion of bandits and puppets is a cause of grief for the entire country, and the Suiyuan soldiers are fighting bloody battles to defend the territory, and it is urgent to provide effective assistance to increase the strength to resist the enemy. Although our member manufacturers are in a time of declining business and financial turnover, and are struggling to cope, the national crisis is unprecedented and the future is dire. Even if we cannot achieve the grand wish of donating generously, we should still donate goods within our ability to provide to the front. According to the investigation, the current urgent needs at the front are winter clothing and goggles, anti-poison masks, treatment drugs, and food, etc. I implore you to consider the scope of production and the needs of the situation, and donate as much as you can. If you are sympathetic, please send the donation to the Suiyuan Anti-Bandit Military Relief and Rescue Association in this city, or send it directly to our association for transfer. We sincerely pray.

Uniform Donation Method: Party and Government Agencies to Confer Today, Suppressing Unauthorized Street Fundraising, and Convening Public Groups to Discuss Unified Organization 107

Since the bandits and puppets willingly flattered foreign powers and, driven by the enemy, invaded the border of Suiyuan with all their might, our nation's citizens have been stirred by righteous indignation, rising up to donate funds to aid and comfort the soldiers suppressing the bandits. Various sectors of our city's populace have successively responded, fervently organizing Suiyuan Support Movements. However, in recent days, many different organizations have been established, and the authority over relief efforts has not been unified, inevitably leading to potential abuses. The party and government agencies of our city, along with various important public groups, recently held a meeting and resolved to suggest that the authorities organize a unified committee to demonstrate solidarity. They also resolved to strictly suppress any street fundraising not authorized by the authorities. A reporter from the Da Gong News Agency learned yesterday from the city's party headquarters that the organization of a unified patriotic donation committee was indeed deemed important in practice. However, to carefully plan detailed procedures, it was decided that an initial exchange of views would take place with the municipal government tomorrow (today). Subsequently, a joint meeting of various important groups would be scheduled to discuss the procedures to demonstrate unity and avoid abuses.

General Federation of Chinese Industries Held Members' Congress The Day Before Yesterday: Telegram to Chairman Chiang and Fu Zuoyi, Vigorously Condemning Bandits and Puppets Invading Suiyuan 110

The General Federation of Chinese Industries held its ninth members' congress at its headquarters at 3 p.m. the day before yesterday. Over 150 people attended, including Mao Yun, a representative from the Central Party Headquarters; Guo Bingwen, a representative from the Ministry of Industry (representing Zhu Xinong); and members Wang Yaochen, Yan Qingxiang, Fan Zhongwen, Gu Bingyuan, Li Wenzhi, Guo Shun, Wu Bosheng, Fang Jiange, Hu Xiyuan, Zhu Gengtao, Wang Yunwu, Zhang Zemin, Zhan Jingtang, Yin Zhizhong, Xiang Kangyuan, Gao Shiheng, Xu Xiaochu, Ren Shigang, Wang Qiyu, Yang Weiyun, Wang Zhisheng, Liu Hongsheng, Qian Chengxu, and Deng Gengxin. The meeting was chaired by a presidium of five people: Guo Shun, Hu Xiyuan, Cai Shengrong, Wang Qiyu, and Zhu Gengtao.

Chairman's Report: After the formalities, Guo Shun first reported, stating briefly that the Federation had been established for eight years and had developed steadily with the assistance of its members. It was an honor that the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Industry had sent representatives to attend and provide guidance at today's meeting. He decided that the three committees—General Affairs, Economy, and Documents—would report on the work, economy, and document management of the past year, and the representatives of the Central Party Headquarters and the Ministry of Industry would deliver speeches (omitted).

Passed Various Resolutions: After discussing the proposals, the following resolutions were adopted: (1) A telegram would be sent to comfort Fu Zuoyi and request that Chairman Chiang vigorously condemn the puppet bandits. Resolved: Passed. (2) Because the flour industry is being manipulated by speculators, speculative transactions should be suppressed. Resolved: Passed and referred to the Executive Committee for handling. (3) The government should be urged to promulgate industrial association laws and regulations as soon as possible. Resolved: Passed in principle and referred to the Executive Committee for handling. (4) Regarding matters requiring clarification by industrial manufacturers from government officials, the government should be petitioned to approve and assign the Federation to handle the matter. Resolved: Passed in principle and referred to the Executive Committee for handling. (5) There should be appropriate relationships and close communication between the General Federation and its branch associations, as well as between the branch associations themselves. Resolved: Passed in principle and referred to the Executive Committee for handling. (6) The government should be advised to find ways to restrict foreigners from establishing factories in the country in order to maintain domestic factories. Resolved: Passed in principle and referred to the Executive Committee for handling. (7) The government should be advised to devise ways to restrict domestic factories from engaging in mutually destructive competition. Resolved: Passed in principle and referred to the Executive Committee for handling. (8) Liu Jingji proposed that the income tax, which will be implemented on January 1st, places extremely strict restrictions on all joint-stock companies. He hoped that the rate would be changed from 5% to 10%, and that since government interest is already extracted, it should not also be taxed on dividends. Resolved: The original proposer was requested to submit a written plan for the Executive Committee to handle. At the same time, six articles of the Federation's charter were revised.

Telegrams Sent to Chiang and Fu: (1) The telegram to Fu Zuoyi, Chairman of the Suiyuan Provincial Government, stated: "The bandit and puppet invasion of the Suiyuan border is of utmost importance to the overall situation. The news has deeply saddened us. Fortunately, you have personally gone to the front lines to supervise the war effort and defend the territory, giving the enemy a head-on blow. The hearts of the entire nation are encouraged. We urge you to continue your efforts, vigorously condemn the bandits, and eliminate them decisively to meet the expectations of the people. In addition to organizing a Suiyuan Support Movement and pledging to support you with all our members, we first send this telegram of comfort. We hope you will consider it. (2) The telegram to Chairman Chiang of the Nanjing Military Commission stated: "The bandit and puppet invasion of the Suiyuan border is of utmost importance to the entire nation. Fortunately, the soldiers of the province have held firm to their duty to defend the territory, giving the enemy a head-on blow. Their loyalty and bravery in serving the country are deeply admired. In addition to organizing a Suiyuan Support Movement and raising funds for comfort, we respectfully implore you, Chairman, to quickly dispatch a large force to vigorously condemn the bandits in order to consolidate the national foundation. The people will be fortunate, and the country will be fortunate."

Swedish Envoy Hörde Returns to Shanghai Yesterday 114

Hörde, the Swedish envoy to China and Japan, retired due to old age and returned to the country. He arrived in Shanghai from Japan on the 14th of this month and went to Beijing to bid farewell to the Chinese central government. After completing his official duties, he arrived in Shanghai from Beijing by train on the morning of the 22nd. After getting off the train, he went straight back to his private residence to rest. He plans to go to Japan in a few days to bring his family back to his country by ship. The Swedish merchants in Shanghai will hold a farewell party for Hörde as his return is imminent.

Huang Bodu Arrived in Shanghai Yesterday: Scheduled to Return to His Post in Four or Five Days; Madam Xu Will Stay in the Country Temporarily 115

Huang Bodu, the secretary of our country's embassy in Japan, went to Beijing some time ago to report on embassy affairs to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs on behalf of Ambassador Xu. After completing his official duties, he arrived in Shanghai from Beijing by overnight train at 7:15 a.m. on the 22nd. He is scheduled to return to Japan from Shanghai by ship in four or five days to resume his post. As for Ambassador Xu's wife, she has decided to stay in the country temporarily to take care of family matters. After Ambassador Xu returns to the country to attend Duan Qirui's state funeral, they will travel to Japan together.

Public Boatmen's Union Submits Petition: Stop the Oppression of Foremen 118

Xinsheng News Agency reports: The public boatmen's union in the fourth district of this city submitted a document to the Social Affairs Bureau yesterday, stating: "Submitting this document for the complete loss of livelihood of the workers, requesting immediate relief, and quickly sending personnel to stop the illegal use of armed force to oppress, ordering the restoration of work for all members, in order to maintain the livelihood of the workers and benefit the labor movement. Our union members have been excessively exploited by the foreman, Li Shibao, and their income is insufficient for survival. We have previously petitioned your bureau to abolish the foreman system, so that wages can be verified and distributed by each business, in order to avoid exploitation. Fortunately, your bureau approved our request and ordered Guangbang Fruit Business United Benefit Hall to comply. However, the foreman refused to accept this and disregarded everything, using armed force to oppress on October 26. On the one hand, he hired new workers from Jiangbei and took the opportunity to seize work, resulting in a bloody tragedy. All the details of what happened have been repeatedly submitted to your bureau for review. The foreman not only disobeyed the orders of your bureau, but also did not resign. Instead, he used armed force to oppress, preventing all members of our union from working, resulting in the complete loss of livelihood for hundreds of workers. If relief is not provided quickly, hundreds of lives will starve to death, or other unfortunate events may occur. We submit this document with the utmost urgency, awaiting your orders."

Strict Prevention of Government Employees Privately Smoking Opium: Central Government Notifies This City's Party Headquarters to Comply: Same Procedures for Party Members and Party Workers 120

Since General Supervisor Chiang actively promoted the ban on smoking and drugs, remarkable results have been achieved. The procedures for government employees who smoke opium are even stricter. Recently, the Opium Suppression General Supervision Department, in order to prevent evasive behavior when conducting investigations of government employees who privately smoke opium, specially formulated three measures, which were submitted to the National Government for promulgation and compliance, and sent to the Central Government for compliance. This city's party headquarters immediately distributed orders to its subordinates to comply. The measures are recorded below: (1) When the head of the government employee's service agency receives the order for investigation, he must immediately order the government employee under investigation to depart from the following day and go to the designated investigation location for investigation. The head of the agency must report the date of departure, but the designated investigation location should be limited to the nearest court from the investigation institution to the service agency. (2) If the government employee under investigation has not reported for investigation one week after the date of departure, it will be deemed as evasion, and the agency that ordered the investigation should investigate at any time and order the head of the agency to dismiss the government employee under investigation and order him to report for investigation, and pay attention to clinical diagnosis for identification. If it is verified that he is addicted, he should be sent to the military law agency for legal punishment. (3) If the government employee under investigation is unable to depart for investigation immediately due to important duties or illness, or if the distance between the service agency and the designated investigation location is more than four days, the head of the agency may, when receiving the order, invite three or more local military and political agencies to extract the urine of the government employee under investigation, put it into a glass bottle, seal it with a wooden stopper and sealing wax, and prepare two copies of the certificate, each indicating the urine of so-and-so. The urine extraction witnesses shall affix their seals on both copies, with one copy attached to the bottle mouth and the other copy submitted with the document for mailing and testing.

Capital Express on the Beijing-Shanghai Railway Readily Prepared; Measures to Maintain Punctuality Notified to All Stations, Ordering Preparations 121

The Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administrations, having received orders to prepare the "Capital Express" on the Beijing-Shanghai line, have successfully completed the joint planning by the Traffic, Mechanical, and other departments. Passenger cars and locomotives have all been assembled at the Wusong Locomotive Factory. Passenger ticket prices and train schedules have been determined by the Traffic Department and will soon be implemented. The Traffic Department of the two railway administrations hereby notifies all stations: It is learned that the Capital Express, which is planned to run on the Beijing-Shanghai line, will soon be implemented. As the speed of this express train is high, attention should be paid to the two key factors of traffic safety and punctuality. All relevant section chiefs of the Traffic Department should meticulously train all train staff and drivers to strictly adhere to regulations and serve diligently. Furthermore, they must be closely supervised at all times to ensure safety. In addition to the detailed measures for the operation of the express train, which will be notified separately in the future, the following are the measures for maintaining punctuality: (1) Before the train arrives at the station, the stationmaster on duty should instruct the relevant staff to be stationed at their service posts and plan and arrange all necessary matters in advance. Luggage and packages for departure should be stacked in suitable locations. The stacking of luggage and packages must have a fixed order and position to avoid difficulties in loading and unloading at the station. Other procedures such as handling, acceptance, and signing should also be expedited. (2) If a large quantity or heavy luggage or packages are being shipped out, sufficient porters should be prepared in advance to quickly move and load them, ensuring that it is completed within the specified time. At the same time, the destination station should be notified to allow for preparation. Once the departure time arrives, loading should be stopped, and the remaining luggage and packages should be left for the next available train. (3) Passengers departing from the station should be informed by the stationmaster on duty, with the assistance of station police and staff, of the appropriate locations to stand, so that they can board the train calmly and avoid rushing around. If they are carrying heavy or a large number of hand luggage and packages, they should be advised to put them in the luggage compartment. Elderly, weak, and slow-moving passengers should be assisted by station staff in boarding the train. If the departure time has arrived, the order to depart should be given immediately. Those who fail to board the train should be advised to take the next available train, and the train should not be stopped again. (4) Before the train arrives at a stopping station, the on-board staff should notify passengers disembarking to prepare in advance to avoid confusion and delay the train schedule. (5) Other trains related to the Capital Express should also strictly maintain their punctuality to avoid hindering the meeting and causing delays. (6) If special circumstances are discovered, other relevant stations should be notified immediately to prepare in advance to avoid delaying the train schedule. All of the above points should be strictly observed. This is to inform the Transportation Section, Business Section, Traffic Section Chiefs of each section of the Beijing-Shanghai line, Stationmasters of each station on the Beijing-Shanghai line, Train conductors on the Beijing-Shanghai line, and (copies sent to) the Mechanical Department and the police station stationed on both railways.
