New Long-Distance Telephone Regulations Set to Take Effect Next Month; Cancellation Procedures Specified; Scheduled Calls Temporarily Postponed 123

The Ministry of Communications' newly revised "Domestic Long-Distance Telephone Business Regulations" will officially take effect on the first day of next month. This new regulation has many improvements. The differences between the new regulations and the old regulations are recorded as follows: (1) When a long-distance call is connected to the called party, and they are already engaged in a local call, the receiving exchange may, with the consent of the called party, interrupt the local call and connect the long-distance call. (2) In the past, a long-distance call to a specific telephone number in a certain location without specifying a particular person to answer the call was referred to as a "number call." Now it is called a "calling number call." Also, in the past, a long-distance call to a specific telephone number in a certain location and specifying a particular person to answer the call was called an "advance notice call." Now it is called a "calling person call." After the calling party has confirmed the "calling number" or "calling person," the type of call will be clearly identifiable at a glance. As for the scheduled call in the old regulations, although it has been renamed a scheduled call, its implementation will be temporarily postponed next month. (3) In the past, those who made an advance notice call had to pay an additional one-third of the ordinary call fee, and those who made a paging call had to pay an additional special fee of one jiao. The new regulations stipulate that the price of a paging call is the same as the price of a calling person call, and no additional special fee will be charged. (4) The cancellation fee in the new regulations is generally lower than that in the old regulations, less than one-third of the cost of a regular number call. (5) The prices specified in the current ordinary telephone price list are for ordinary number calls. The prices for paging calls, calling person calls, and cancellation fees must be consulted in the "Domestic Long-Distance Telephone Classification Price Comparison Table." (6) Cancellation fees for ordinary number calls during daytime will be charged. (7) The scope of paging is limited to three kilometers, a reduction of two kilometers compared to the past. (8) After placing a call, the calling party may change the type of call before receiving a connection notification, but only from ordinary to urgent and from number call to calling person. (9) The calling party of a calling person call may, in addition to specifying one called party, also specify one representative of the called party. (10) After the calling party has registered the call, if the line is congested and the ordinary call has been waiting for two hours (previously four hours) or the urgent call has been waiting for one hour (previously two hours) without being connected, the cancellation fee may be waived. (11) During busy hours, the number of consecutive calls will be limited to three.

Report from Consulate in Honolulu: World Tea Market Conditions; October Sees Sharp Increase in Chinese Tea Exports 125

Chinese tea has historically held an important position in the international market. However, in the past half-century, it has gradually declined. Recently, the Chinese people have gradually become aware of the need for improvement. With the unified control of Anhui black tea exports and the Commercial Inspection Bureau handling on-site inspections to ensure quality, exports this month have improved compared to previous months. Details are as follows:

Fierce Competition in the World Market

According to a report from our consulate in Honolulu to the International Trade Bureau, Chinese tea is gradually losing its advantage in the US tea market and will be eliminated by Japanese, Indian, Ceylon, and Javanese teas. There is an urgent need to catch up. The US is the second-largest tea market in the world. However, Chinese tea exports to the US currently account for only about 9% of the total. Americans who drink tea value quality and do not pay attention to economy. Therefore, our country must urgently improve quality to have any hope. Promotion is also important. The four tea-producing countries of India, Ceylon, Java, and Sumatra are planning to jointly raise 100,000 English pounds to conduct large-scale promotions in the four regions of East, Southeast, West, and Central China, holding lectures in schools and hotels for competitive sales, seeking to expand their scope and eliminate tea sales from other countries. This is worth noting. Furthermore, Americans have different preferences for tea: (1) Philadelphia prefers Fuzhou tea. (2) New York and Boston prefer Taiwanese Oolong. (3) Pennsylvania and New Jersey, as well as various states in the eastern US, prefer Oolong, whether Chinese or Taiwanese. (4) The western US and northern border provinces prefer Japanese tea. (5) The central states prefer Chinese tea. It is hoped that domestic tea merchants will pay attention.

Chinese Tea Exports Improve in October

The International Trade Bureau has released statistics. Tea exports in October of this year totaled 3,636.86 kilograms to the United States, 330.79 kilograms to Canada, 165.04 kilograms to France, 528.01 kilograms to Germany, 1,947.27 kilograms to the United Kingdom, 532.91 kilograms to the Netherlands, 582.89 kilograms to the Soviet Union, 6,509.91 kilograms to Morocco, 1,550.99 kilograms to Algeria, 413.95 kilograms to Tunisia, 858.10 kilograms to Africa and other regions, 22.25 kilograms to India, 1,585.31 kilograms to Hong Kong, and 954.94 kilograms to other countries, totaling 19,826.23 kilograms. This includes 12,320.67 kilograms of green tea, 6,276.42 kilograms of black tea, and 1,229.14 kilograms of other teas. This is a slight increase compared to the total exports of 19,751.65 kilograms in the same month last year. The cumulative total for the first ten months of this year is 227,314.21 kilograms, an increase of 81,238.42 kilograms compared to 145,085.79 kilograms in the same period last year.

Southern Steamers Freely Anchoring; Customs Notice Forbids 126

Port Master Tebeck of the Jianghai Customs has issued Notice No. 19 regarding the prohibition of ships using their own anchors to moor in the Huangpu River and Wusong River: "It has been found that ships entering the Huangpu River between sunset and sunrise, unless directly heading to a designated wharf or a mooring place assigned by this department, are not allowed, as per this department's Notice No. 16 of the 15th year of the Republic. Now, in view of the fact that ships moored with their own anchors may endanger navigation due to wind or tide, all ships with automatic engines, except as specifically provided in Article 2 (A) of the Shanghai Port Management Regulations, are henceforth prohibited from mooring with their own anchors in the Huangpu River. Furthermore, if such ships do not have mooring places at the existing buoys and wharves between the Wusong Lighthouse and the Wusong River, they should moor outside the mouth of the Wusong River. All ship owners are hereby ordered to comply. This notice is hereby issued."

Six Foremen Dismissed, Xihe Factories Strike Again Yesterday; Workers Present Nine Demands to Factory; Toyota and Other Factories Announce Resumption of Work Today 129

According to Xin Sheng News Agency, the labor dispute at the Japanese cotton mills remains unresolved. The Xihe factories went on strike again yesterday due to the dismissal of six foremen. Toyota and other cotton factories have announced that they will resume work today. The details are reported separately as follows:

Refusal to Eat and Shutdown

The strike of 3,400 workers at the Xihe First, Second, and Third factories, located at 74 Rue Robert, was resolved after mediation by Tan Baoshou, chief of the Caojiadu Public Security Branch, Wang Xianqing, director of the Mediation Division of the Social Affairs Bureau, and various foremen. Work resumed on the evening of the 20th and the morning of the 21st. However, the workers expressed dissatisfaction because the management refused to meet their demands for eating and taking breaks.

Foremen Dismissed

At the same time, the factory issued a notice stating that the foremen Wang Han, Chen Guoyu, Li Baoquan, Zhou Daosheng, Yu Shoufan, and Sun Dequan were the instigators of the workers' strike. Therefore, they were dismissed and ordered to move out of the factory quarters by 5:00 p.m. on the 25th. The factory hoped that other workers would continue to work peacefully and not be misled by outsiders.

Strike Declared Again

Workers at the Xihe First, Second, and Third factories went on strike again yesterday in protest of the factory's refusal to meet their demands for eating and taking breaks and the dismissal of Wang Han and others, in order to urge the factory to realize its errors. At the same time, the names of all 3,400 workers were copied and sent to the management, stating that if the management wanted to dismiss Wang Han and the other six, they should dismiss all 3,400 workers.

Nine Demands Presented

After the workers at the First, Second, and Third factories went on strike, they held a meeting in the factory quarters at 4:00 p.m. yesterday. As a result of the discussions, they presented nine demands to the management: (1) Increase wages by 10%. (2) Allow 30 minutes for eating breaks. (3) For work on Sundays, workers should only work from 6:00 p.m. on Saturday to 6:00 a.m. on Sunday and should not work any longer (because they usually have to work until 12:00 a.m.). (4) Workers who work for half a month without stopping will receive an additional day of paid leave. (5) Workers should not be forced to work arbitrarily. (6) If new workers are hired, they should be recruited from the workers within the factory quarters. (7) Provide a rice subsidy of five jiao per month. (8) Workers should not be dismissed or driven out of the cooking areas in the factory quarters. (9) The personnel manager, Ikeda, should be dismissed immediately. If he is not dismissed, they vow not to resume work.

Petition to the Social Affairs Bureau This Morning

After the meeting, the workers immediately submitted the nine demands to the management, requesting their approval. However, there were no results. Therefore, the workers held another meeting at 6:00 p.m., and each factory appointed six representatives, for a total of 18, who were scheduled to submit a petition to the Social Affairs Bureau at 8:00 a.m. this morning, requesting the authorities to negotiate with the management and secure their agreement to these nine measures. If the management refuses, they are determined to continue the strike.

Notice of Resumption of Work This Morning

The workers' strike at the Toyota First and Second factories on Zhongyou Road has been going on for several days. After mediation by Mr. Du Yuesheng, the labor and management sides have also come closer to an agreement. In addition, the Toyota Interior and Exterior Cotton First and Second factories at 62 Rue Robert, which had stopped work due to a small number of workers, and the Toyota Interior and Exterior Cotton factories, yesterday simultaneously announced that they would resume work as usual at 6:00 a.m. this morning. The workers' side has also decided to resume work at that time.

Total Recovery in Pudong

In the Pudong area, the Shanghai First, Second, Third, Fourth, Fifth, and Sixth factories, which had suspended work the day before yesterday, resumed work as usual yesterday. Other factories, such as Gongda, Yufeng, Tongxing, Dakang, and Donghua, also resumed work as usual, and all workers returned to work. After the dispute was resolved, the original situation has now been restored.

Dafu Plumbing Engineering Company's Fraudulent Behavior Towards Customers 130

Wu Baogen, a resident of Kongjia Lane in the Ximen Cheng Bing area, and Ding Axin, who operates a new ceremonial hall at 45 West Heng Street, Dongjiadu, both entrusted Dafu Plumbing Engineering Company to install water pipes for them to receive running water, paying deposit fees and water connection fees, etc. However, after many days, the water connection was delayed. After inquiring with the inland water company, they learned that the fees they had entrusted the plumbing company to pay had not been sent. Wu and Ding then reported to the Municipal Public Utility Bureau for relief. The bureau dispatched personnel to investigate on the 7th of this month. It was found that the company's director, Zhu Wenhao, had not been to the shop for two days, and his family had moved out a month ago. His plumbing business license was taken away by Zhu's father, Ciqing (the shop owner reported at the time of registration). At the time, only two workers, Shen Baoyuan and Zhu Shanyong, were minding the shop. When asked about the shop owner collecting deposit fees from customers and delaying the water connection, the workers did not deny it. The bureau then dispatched personnel to take one of the workers, Zhu Shanyong, into temporary custody at the Wenmiao Road Police Station of the Public Security Bureau and reported the findings to the bureau for review. The bureau concluded that the plumbing engineering company had indeed engaged in fraudulent behavior, which was illegal. It immediately ordered the company to temporarily surrender its plumbing business license and the licenses of the plumbers it employed to the bureau within [blank] days and to promptly return the deposit fees paid by the Wu and Ding families. At the same time, it sent a letter to the Wenmiao Road Police Station of the Public Security Bureau, requesting that the worker Zhu Shanyong be released on bail and ordering the company to remove its signboard and cease operations immediately to prevent citizens from being deceived again.

Wu Jinbao, a woman from Wusong in her thirties, had an opium addiction, which she changed to eating red pills, and recently switched to injecting morphine. The woman is a prostitute and somewhat attractive, wearing fashionable clothes and shoes. Every night, she secretly works as a goddess in various hotels, often soliciting tourists in the Yangshupu area. Room 5 of the Dongfang Hotel at No. 26, Lane 642, East-West Huade Road, is her den for injecting morphine. This was discovered by Sun Baoshan, a Chinese detective of the Huishan Police Station. At 9:50 p.m. the night before last, he rushed to Room 26 of the Dongfang Hotel and arrested the injector, Xu Fukai, and Wu Jinbao, and brought them, along with a syringe and three small packages of morphine, to the police station for detention. Yesterday, they were sent to the Third Criminal Court of the First Special District Court. Zhang Shizhu, a lawyer from the Public Works Department, explained the case. After inquiring about the matter, he presented the evidence and questioned the two defendants, whose confessions were evasive. Judge Zhong Qing sentenced Xu Fukai to seven years in prison and Wu Jinbao to one year and six months. Before serving their sentences, they were sent to a drug rehabilitation hospital for a detention period of no more than two months. The evidence was confiscated.

Automatic Traffic Lights in Operation at Fuzhou Road and Jiangxi Road; Green to Yellow, Yellow to Red, Red to Green; Drivers Must Quickly Proceed When Yellow and Signal with Hands 134

The traffic lights at the intersection of Fuzhou Road and Jiangxi Road in the Public Concession will be changed to automatic operation starting today. The difference from the original traffic lights is that the colors were originally only red and green and were managed by the police. Now they have been changed to automatic and do not require police management. The signal light changes from green to yellow, from yellow to red, and then from red back to green. When the light is green, vehicles can proceed straight through. When a vehicle approaching the intersection encounters a yellow light, it must quickly proceed to allow vehicles on the other intersecting road to proceed. If a vehicle needs to turn right, the driver must first signal the direction of travel with their hand and turn along the central pillar. It is not necessary to turn around the pillar as before. In areas where automatic traffic lights are in use, all drivers must pay special attention to the provisions of Article 31 of the traffic regulations, namely, to signal the direction of travel with their hand at all times to facilitate the passage of vehicles behind them. It is reported that these traffic lights are still being tested and will gradually be installed on major roads.

Runaway Concubine Returns - Husband Doesn't Pursue - Court Pronounces Suspended Sentence 136

Jia Rongxiang, 42 years old, a Tianjin native and the owner of Shuang Yongxing Hardware Store at No. 10 Ningbo Road in the French Concession, took Yu Wang Hongmei, also known as Di Xiuying (22 years old this year), a woman from Liyang, as his concubine from a brothel three years ago. They did not formally marry but began living together at the store. Recently, Di became restless and secretly started a new relationship. On October 8th, while Jia was away in Tianjin, she took all of her clothing and cash, totaling over 1,900 yuan, and secretly ran away to live elsewhere. When Jia returned to Shanghai from Tianjin, he discovered the theft and reported it to the French Concession police, offering a reward for her capture through newspaper advertisements. After Di learned of this, fearing complications, she returned at the beginning of this month with the stolen items. Jia did not report the case closure to the police. This was discovered by Detective Qin Youyu and Detective Tao Ronglin, who arrested Di Xiuying and sent her to the Special No. 2 Court for investigation. The police department prosecuted her for theft. During the trial, the plaintiff stated that the defendant had returned all the items she had taken and that he intended to report the case closure to the police. The detectives had already arrested the defendant, and he now did not want to pursue the matter further. The defendant claimed she had taken the items back to her mother's house and was not attempting theft or escape. Judge Zhu Chuzhe reviewed the statements and deemed it appropriate to conclude the case. The verdict was handed down on the morning of the day before yesterday, sentencing Di Xiuying to two months imprisonment for theft, with a two-year suspended sentence.

To encourage youth to become familiar with national geography, the Shanghai Youth Association held a map drawing competition at the Sichuan Road Youth Association Middle School yesterday morning starting at 9:00 AM. Over 220 participating youth, including Ma Xiehe and Chen Longcai, competed in nine rooms. The competition was divided into two types: memory drawing and drawing. Participants were required to draw a complete map of the country, including provinces, railways, major rivers, important cities, and marking the main products of each province. Participants could draw this map at home and submit it to the association. According to Judge Huang Jingwan, after the competition ends today, the judging committee will begin evaluating the entries. The results will be published in the newspaper in about ten days. The judging criteria are divided into accuracy, importance, neatness, and completeness, etc. Memory drawing accounts for 60% of the score, and drawing accounts for 40%. The top ten winners will receive prize money, and the eleventh to thirtieth winners will receive books. Beixin Bookstore Sues Longhu Bookstore for Pirating Lu Xun's Books - Beixin Claims Losses of Over Ten Thousand Yuan and Requests Compensation - Case Granted Postponement Due to Outside Mediation 144

Since the passing of literary giant Mr. Lu Xun, his posthumous works have been extremely popular. Recently, Beixin Bookstore, represented by lawyer Sun Zuji, filed a lawsuit in the First Special District District Court against Zhang Xinshan of Longhu Bookstore on Shandong Road for copyright infringement, claiming that Beixin had signed contracts with Lu Xun to publish all of his books during his lifetime, and had obtained copyright registration certificates from the Ministry of Interior. These books were widely sold. However, the defendant, intending to gain illegal profits, arbitrarily altered the titles of the books and privately printed and sold them, infringing on the copyright. The plaintiff requested that the defendant be summoned to court and severely punished according to law, and that his counterfeit books be confiscated. Since the defendant infringed on the copyright, the sales of the original books have sharply declined, resulting in losses totaling over ten thousand yuan. The plaintiff also requested that the defendant be ordered to pay compensation. Yesterday afternoon, Judge Pan opened the court to hear the case. The plaintiff's lawyer, Sun Zuji, completed his statement of the indictment and stated that the case was currently being mediated outside the court, requesting a postponement. The court then ordered a postponement to the afternoon of the 24th of this month for a retrial.

Page 13

Settlement of Interest on Repayment of Loan - Legal Issues Arise - Shen Yuqing Files for Retrial 150

Zhang Jinkun and Shen Yuqing had a loan dispute, and Zhang filed a lawsuit against Shen in the First Special District District Court. The case has already been judged in two trials, ordering Shen to repay the principal of 500 yuan, and interest calculated at 1.5% per month from the date the loan was established to the date of execution. This case is considered to be of minimal value, and according to law, two trials are the final verdict. Therefore, Shen intends to repay the principal and interest. However, when calculating the amount, he found some flaws in the interest part: (1) If the judgment is to be fulfilled, calculated from January 1, 1926, the date the loan was established, to the date of the second instance judgment of the High Court, it would require more than 610 yuan. This is more than 100 yuan more than the regulations of Article 5 of the Civil Code and the Implementation Law of the Clearing Debt Section, as well as the precedents of the Supreme Court of one interest per principal. If calculated to the date of execution, the amount exceeded would be even greater. (2) The loan was originally a fixed-term loan with a term of one year. Zhang only filed a lawsuit five years after the expiration of the term, and never demanded payment before the lawsuit. Therefore, the interest within the overdue period is also worthy of research. Now Shen believes that the above two points have not been properly considered before, so he is still unwilling to accept the final judgment. However, according to law, this case can only be tried in two trials, and it is impossible to appeal to the first instance again. To seek relief, it is inconvenient to raise an objection to the execution court, and it is also inappropriate to file a lawsuit to confirm the interest separately. After discussing with others, it was decided to request the High Court of the original trial to apply the provisions of Articles 492, 3, and 4 of the retrial procedure, that is, to retrial the case. Currently, what is being contested is purely a legal question. I don't know if a retrial can be granted.

The number of members has reached more than 30, and those who are requesting to join are still very enthusiastic and are being reviewed and confirmed one by one. The articles of association are recorded below: (1) This association is named the Gaoqiao Youth Return-to-Homeland Association. (2) The purpose of this association is to connect feelings, study academics, and assist the prosperity and progress of enterprises in this township. (3) Any Gaoqiao youth living abroad with lofty ideals, regardless of gender or occupation, can join this association as a member. (4) Members must abide by the articles of association of this association, adhere to the discipline of this association, and take on all work in their spare time. (5) This association will hold a general meeting of members every two months to report on the daily lives of members and discuss all progress matters. Those who do not have important matters and request leave of absence by letter shall not be absent without reason. (6) The membership fee of this association is temporarily set at two yuan per month, collected quarterly. When necessary, temporary fees may be levied with the approval of the general meeting of members. (7) If members do not abide by the articles of association, damage the reputation of the association, or engage in improper behavior, they will be expelled with the approval of the general meeting of members. (8) This association shall have one chairman and one vice-chairman each, who shall preside over all internal and external affairs of the association. The general secretary shall preside over all daily affairs. The term of office is three months and may be re-elected. (9) The affairs of this association are temporarily divided into three groups: sports group, music group, and literature and art group. Each group shall have one group leader to preside over the group affairs, and depending on the factual needs, the chairman shall appoint one to two staff members to assist in the business. (10) The officers of this association are all voluntary positions. (11) This association will compile and issue a "Member Directory" once every six months to communicate information. (12) The address of this association is located in the Rural Improvement Association. (13) If there are any shortcomings, they may be amended with the approval of the general meeting of members. (14) These articles of association shall be implemented after being approved by the general meeting of members.

New Nanking Road - Giving Alms Tokens to Beggars 155

Shops on New Nanking Road in the Public Concession, due to the recent economic downturn and the sight of numerous beggars on the streets, begging from door to door, and demanding money aggressively, found it unbearable. Therefore, the 16th District Civic Association recently produced a type of alms token, resembling the water tokens used at tiger stove businesses. They are stamped with "New Nanking Road Alms Token 4 Cash" and "16th District Civic Association" on the back. These have been distributed to the shops. After beggars obtain these tokens, they can redeem them for copper coins at the 16th District Civic Association. However, after the issuance of these tokens, shops generally say that since each token is only worth 4 small cash and requires a trip to the Civic Association for redemption, a lot of beggars are unwilling to take them, throwing the tokens back. Therefore, this may reduce the number of beggars.

At 8:50 AM yesterday morning, a fire broke out in the attic room of Zha Yuan, a local resident (41 years old, working in the circulation department of a certain newspaper for many years) at No. 7, Sanxing Lane, Scissor Bridge, Humin South Zhelu Road in the South City. The fire quickly spread through the roof. The beat police immediately summoned the Ganqu District fire truck, which arrived and extinguished the fire after forty minutes. As a result, the attic room was burned, and the adjacent attic room at No. 6 was also affected. The fire starter was taken to the Xidou Sub-Bureau by the police. According to the confession, his elderly mother, who is a Buddhist, lit incense candles in the attic room in the early morning before going downstairs for breakfast. The candles were knocked over by her pet cat, and a spark of fire started a conflagration.

Letter Requesting Issuance of License for Distribution of Narcotics - New Drug Association Submits to Health Department 167

The New Drug Industry Association submitted a letter to the Ministry of Health of the Executive Yuan yesterday, stating: "Shanghai is a commercial hub. Hospitals and pharmacies in the interior need narcotics and narcotic preparations, most of which are purchased from Shanghai. Since the establishment of the Ministry's Narcotics Management Office, all purchasers of narcotics must apply directly to the Management Office, and all pharmacies have been notified to comply. Recently, pharmacies have repeatedly stated that purchasing these drugs from Beijing is far away, the procedures are complicated, and postal delivery is delayed, often causing delays and hindering the market, which affects the lives of patients. We request that you consider the difficulties of business and establish a sub-management office in Shanghai and issue a distribution license, so that nearby purchases can be made and directly mailed to various locations, to avoid detours." Upon discussion at the meeting, the points mentioned are indeed factual, and it is appropriate to submit a document to the Ministry of Health for review and approval of the request for public convenience. Shanghai's Enamel Industry (Continued) (XXXIX of Shanghai Industry and Commerce Overview) 175

— Edited by China Credit Information

The production process of enamel products can be divided into nine steps: 1. Making the blank, that is, assembling iron sheets into iron pieces, placing them on various types of ramming machines to form various models, such as cups, plates, basins, and bowls, then polishing them or welding them. 2. Making powder, that is, mixing raw materials such as feldspar and clay according to a formula, then grinding them through a spring mortar and other procedures, and then placing them in cold water for six hours to obtain crystalline powder blocks of various colors. Enamel powder is made by grinding this powder block with water. 3. Washing the blank, that is, removing impurities from the iron blank. One method is to burn it off with furnace fire, and the other is to wash it with 12% sulfuric acid to prepare it for enameling. 4. Enameling, that is, applying the slurry-like enamel powder to the dry and clean iron blank and then baking it in a hot fire of about 1,000 degrees to form a plain enamel product. 5. Artification, if necessary, the completed plain enamel product still needs to go through lettering, painting, and spraying to beautify it.

2. Past and Present of Shanghai's Enamel Industry Enamel products were originally imported goods. In the past, the annual import value was always between three and four million yuan, a substantial leakage. In recent years, due to the patriotic imitation of manufacturing by Chinese people, the annual imports have been no more than one million yuan, a decrease of two-thirds or three-quarters compared to the past, which is a major progress in China's industry. Nineteen of China's self-operated enamel factories are concentrated in Shanghai. Shanghai's existence of enamel factories has only been about twenty years. In 1916, an American (named McCree) first established a large factory in Gujia, Zhabei, specializing in the production of enamel mouth cups and food utensils. Later, due to unfamiliarity with Chinese business conditions, the factory was taken over by Shanghai merchant Xu Daosheng and others, and reorganized into the Zhufeng Enamel Company, and the scope of business was also expanded compared to the past. By the spring of 1924, the factory was taken over by Tong Shiheng of Jiading, renamed Zhufeng Tongji Enamel Company, and has remained so to this day. In addition, when the Guangda factory had not yet been reorganized, a Guangda factory followed, but it closed down after only a few months. Dong Jifu of Suzhou took over the remaining business and reorganized it into Yifeng Enamel Factory. Subsequently, Dingfeng Enamel Factory west of Xin Zha Bridge, Hongkou Industrial and Commercial Company jointly operated by Chinese and Japanese merchants, and the enamel department attached to the Chinese Vocational School also rose up one after another. From 1927 to 1929, Rixin Enamel Factory and Huafeng Enamel Factory also followed, but except for Huafeng, the rest did not develop and grow. Those not closing down were reorganized. As for small factories that appeared briefly, such as Hengfeng, Huasheng, Yaohua, Zhenhua, Yonghe, and Dafeng, they are even less worth mentioning. Therefore, at present, the enamel factories in Shanghai with larger scale, better equipment, and wider sales are only Zhufeng, Huafeng, Yifeng, and Zhonghua, about seven or eight factories in total. Now, their individual status is selected and allocated below:

Anecdotes from History (Yan Chonglou) 180

The progress of human thought is also the elevation of social status. The loss of thought in the world is greater than the loss of all material things.

There are more useful thoughts buried in the world than there are useful thoughts that have been realized.

We cannot estimate how much benefit society would gain if all the good thoughts of people were brought out.

People's thoughts are generally the same for good concepts, and generally the same for bad concepts.

Many people only know the poverty of lacking money, but do not know the poverty of lacking thought!

If thought has not increased, and there is only more income of money, it is still just a fool.

The vast world cannot be governed by narrow thoughts. The beautiful world cannot be stained by wrong thoughts.

The life of the world depends on thought. Thought can make the world a hell, and it can also make the world a paradise.

Anecdotes of Executive Duan (Qing Qu) 181

Mr. Duan Zhiquan passed away in Shanghai, and people at home and abroad mourned him. His outstanding political achievements are countless, a true great man of his time. Now, some anecdotes of his life are recorded as follows, hoping to satisfy those who admire him.

Mr. Duan first graduated from the Beiyang Military Academy in the eleventh year of Emperor Guangxu's reign. Afterwards, he traveled to Germany and studied military science in Berlin. Not long after, he returned to China, and Yuan Shikai of Xiangcheng established the Beiyang New Army, training soldiers in Xiaozhan. Mr. Duan was appointed as the commander of the first artillery battalion and superintendent of the Army Academy. During the reign of Emperor Xuantong, he was appointed as the Jiangbei Regional Commander. It was said that the position of Jiangbei Regional Commander was a stepping stone to promotion. Wang Shizhen also ascended from this position to guard the capital, and everyone congratulated Mr. Duan. Subsequently, Mr. Duan was ordered to enter Beijing and gradually rose to power in the military. However, after Mr. Duan left office, he was succeeded by Lei Zhenchun, who ultimately failed due to bribery. The land was not unlucky, but the person was not outstanding, and people laughed at it.

When the European War broke out, some people criticized Mr. Duan for declaring war without actually fighting. However, his efforts did enhance China's international standing, which was no small achievement. People called him "Mr. Ganmu" because, at that time, those around him were engaging in infighting. Figures like Xu Shuzheng and Jin Yunpeng were all Mr. Duan's advisors, but they could not avoid conflicts due to power struggles, which also cannot be concealed for the sake of virtuous men. In the autumn of the changing political situation, those in power in the former capital often suffered from two common ailments: selfishness and extravagance. Selfishness led them to make decisions based on personal likes and dislikes, blurring the lines between the virtuous and the treacherous. Extravagance led them to squander resources, causing the national treasury to dwindle. Although the political manifestations of these two ailments differed, the suffering was the same. Mr. Duan did not pursue vain fame but sought practical results. In the late Qing Dynasty and early Republic, he was one of the best among the mediocre officials.

During the second and third years of the Republic, it was very common to hold birthday celebrations for officials. Figures like Yang Xizi and Liang Rengong used their family celebrations as an excuse to hold banquets and operas for days, with congratulatory gifts often amounting to hundreds of gold coins. Extravagance reached an extreme, as if they could not show off to society or entertain their relatives without doing so. At that time, Mr. Duan was approaching his fiftieth birthday, and his subordinates wanted to celebrate his birthday. Mr. Duan was furious upon hearing this and personally wrote a letter to Xu Shuzheng, saying, "Brother Youzheng, I recently saw a report about celebrating my birthday, which is truly ignorant of the big picture. We are constantly worried about failing to achieve our goals, even while enduring hardship. The stove fire is blazing, and we are still enjoying playing with the pot. Our achievements are unremarkable, and our transgressions are increasing. How can we explain ourselves to the world? Since the literary association has been established, we should not engage in excessive actions. There is no need to write essays and compile them into volumes. I have already received many gifts. I hope you will treat me with virtue and kindly decline the offers from our friends. If you do that, my heart will be at ease. I can only ask you to issue an order to prohibit it. We have known each other for many years, and you should trust me deeply. Please make corrections and offer your best wishes. Greetings, Duan Zhiquan." From this, we can see Mr. Duan's integrity, which is hard to find today.

Cartoon Map (Qiu Shen) 182

Returning from the cartoon exhibition, what constantly echoes in my mind are several cartoon maps.

One is Gao Longsheng's "The Country is Broken, But the Mountains and Rivers Remain." The picture is extremely simple. On plain paper, only the edges of a black Begonia leaf are drawn. The entire leaf is dyed red. The heartbroken author has broken through many stinging holes in the northeastern corner of the red leaf. Do not misunderstand that this piece of song paper is an abandoned remnant painting. This is an antique of thousands of years, trampled on by fierce and greedy wolves!

The author of "Solar Eclipse Picture" is Liu Yi. The meaning of the picture is that the moon covers the sun and becomes a partial eclipse. I am glad that this trip was not in vain.

The host's cultivation of chrysanthemums has its own unique approach, generally divided into two categories. One category consists of large potted chrysanthemums, with some having over a hundred blooms, all full like the prime of youth, piled up like mountains, and dazzlingly bright. The other category consists of single chrysanthemums in small jars, about the same height, with flowers larger than bowls, all full of vitality, each with its own unique and proud appearance. Therefore, the thatched hut is full of vitality, forming a separate world within the three hundred acres of vegetable gardens, forests, and trees.

This is the way of heaven, the power of the soil, and the labor of man, and none can be missing." Huang's chrysanthemums are worthy of this description without shame. Moreover, the host knows the nature of chrysanthemums, can obtain seeds for planting, and can use bee media for hybridization, with new flowers every year, which is in line with the science of eugenics, which Zhang did not achieve.

Shou Juan also loves flowers like his life, hence the name "Flower Fool of Wumen." He lingered, reluctant to leave. The host said that there are still dozens of plants left in the fields, to be enjoyed with plum blossoms next spring. This is enough to boast about the creation of art.

The host is fifty-six years old, talks jovially, and is hospitable. Upon parting, he warmly said that the chrysanthemums have not yet faded. If any friends have a hermit's inclination, they are welcome to come in these months, and I will greet them with open arms.

Special Feature: Morning View of Hongkou Park (Yafei) 189

Facing the rustling morning breeze, under the hazy morning mist, I carried a "Selection of Modern Essays" and walked onto that murderous Jiangwan Road. As usual, what appeared before my eyes first was that shocking monster, its terrible blood basin mouth wide open, as if it wanted to swallow the world.

On the side of the road, the rows of trees lining the road were like sentry guards standing in formation, densely arranged; next to it was a place for "allies' warriors" to "return their souls," but in front of the park gate was quiet, unlike some days when you could see several "allied women" wearing black dresses going inside to bow ninety-something degrees to offer flowers.

The whistle of the North Railway Station pierced the static air, causing those wanderers who had been drifting in foreign lands for a long time, or the travelers who were singing farewell songs, to stir up endless melancholy in their lonely hearts!

Stepping on the fallen leaves blown down by the autumn wind, it felt as if I was treading on my own heart, making me feel helpless: Although I was still walking forward step by step, I had lost the courage to move forward. I doubted in my heart, thinking that I was no longer in the beautiful Jiangnan, but had arrived in the north under the assault of storms, no, I even suspected that I had left the ancient country with more than 4,000 years of history. But in the end, with that tense and fearful heart, I quietly passed through the bayonets of the "allied warriors" and walked to the entrance of Hongkou Park, took out my "pass" from my pocket, waved it at the patrolman watching, and then slipped in sideways. It has been more than a month since I last came to Hongkou Park; in the past, when I lived on Di Siwei Road, this place had almost become my family garden. Reading in the morning, fishing at noon, walking in the evening, I spent more than a third of my time here every day. Sometimes, I would talk with a few friends inside, or have a disorganized picnic. But now, the distance from my address is of course one reason, but there is also the fact that I really don't have the courage to run to this terrible place.

What I saw today was the same soft, grassy lawns, winding paths, clear and calm ponds, withered and haggard lotus, scattered forests, and intricately decorated flowers as before. There was not much change, but the situation in the park was obviously a bit "desolate in front of the door"! In such a large park, in addition to many majestic "armed allied comrades" and "allied men and women," there were also a few "foreign gentlemen" playing golf. I didn't meet a single one of our own compatriots. I silently walked along the small river, as if I were a ghost in a desolate tomb, and an unnamed feeling had secretly climbed into my subconscious mind. I didn't understand what kind of world it was now. Is it civilization? Is it considered civilized behavior to forcibly snatch other people's things and make them your own, and not allow others to shout a word of "no"? Is it barbarism? But they all wear a good-looking mask and put on a civilized coat, making people deceived without knowing it. If it weren't for people in civilized countries, how could there be such superb skills?

With a melancholic mood, I sat down on the edge of a pond with my limp limbs, but the sadness of a slave could not disappear in my heart: Watching the "allied children" leisurely fishing for shrimp by the pond for fun, I felt as ashamed as if I had been slapped twice in the face, and this shame would never let me forget it.

Past wounds, current impressions, I really dare not think about it, so, I slipped out of the gate of Hongkou Park as if I were escaping.

Two Major Reasons for the Development of Modern Income Tax 193

— Gu Lingyun

— Wartime Finance and Social Policy —

Since its emergence in England in 1798, income tax has been adopted by countries worldwide. Over the past century, its rapid development and widespread implementation have far surpassed other types of taxes. In modern times, it has gradually become the central pillar of the tax system in most countries. Examining the reasons for its development, one aspect is the inherent qualities of income tax as a good tax, while the objective reason lies in the evolution of the social economy. Since the late 18th century, European countries have been plagued by frequent wars. From the Napoleonic Wars to the Crimean War, the Franco-Prussian War, and finally, World War I, unrest has been constant for over a century. Even in peacetime, all political organizations and economic systems are preparing for war, so it would not be an exaggeration to call it the "century of war." In this environment, the fiscal policies of various countries have focused on expanding military preparations in peacetime and planning wartime expenditures, with little else worth mentioning. Expanding military preparations in peacetime allows for leisurely planning of expenses, and the amounts are not fixed, allowing for adjustments based on the financial situation. However, planning wartime expenditures involves huge amounts and urgent needs, which was the most difficult challenge for those in charge of finance at the time. Therefore, contemporary financiers focused on the problem of how to increase taxes to make the people bear the burden of war expenses. But increasing taxes requires a sound tax system, and thus, the most flexible and universal income tax was gradually discovered. Only income tax can meet the needs of war by raising its tax rate to increase substantial revenue. Therefore, tracing the origins of income tax historically reveals that it was promoted by wartime finance; the evolution of income tax indeed corresponds to wartime finance like a drum responds to a stick. Let's briefly discuss the historical facts of income tax in England to illustrate this point:

England is the birthplace of income tax, so the history of income tax in England is also a typical example of income tax history. In 1798, during the Anglo-French War, England had to strive to increase tax revenue to plan for war expenses. However, the British tax system at the time centered on customs duties, excise taxes, and land taxes. Due to the impact of the war, these not only failed to increase revenue but also showed a declining trend. Raising tax rates would place an excessive burden on the general poor. Therefore, a temporary tax was specially levied on the wealthy class to obtain financial revenue. This temporary tax was called Triple Assessment at the time, which was the predecessor of today's income tax. The temporary tax was a one-time levy on the wealthy class during wartime, so it was abolished immediately after the end of the war.

In 1803, the Anglo-French War resumed, and the temporary income tax was adopted again. Significant reforms were made to the tax law, such as expanding the scope of taxation, reducing tax rates, and setting tax exemption points and deductions, already embodying the spirit of modern income tax. This tax law was abolished after the end of the Anglo-French War in 1815.

Subsequently, the Indian Rebellion and the Crimean War occurred successively, and income tax continued to be implemented with the wars. Due to the annual improvements in the tax law and the cultivation of people's tax-paying habits, the revenue from income tax increased year by year, gradually occupying an important position in finance. Without income tax, the British finances could not have been sustained. Therefore, income tax transformed from a temporary tax into a permanent tax, becoming an important part of the structure of the British tax system.

When World War I broke out, the British income tax experienced another leap forward. Following the principle of "one-third of duties borne by taxes," income tax became the central pillar of the tax system. Just looking at the tax revenue from income tax before and after the war is enough to show its rapid development and important position.

Period　Income Tax Revenue　Percentage of Total Tax Revenue

Pre-war (1913)　£47,249,000　29%

Post-war (1919)　£359,095,000　45%

From the origin and evolution of income tax in England mentioned above, it is clear that it advanced and retreated entirely with wartime finance. The reason for this is that income tax itself possesses various conditions for wartime finance, which can be summarized as follows:

Income tax is levied based on each individual's ability to pay, enabling different classes with varying degrees of wealth to have their tax burden capacity set at the same level. Therefore, unless the ability to pay of each individual reaches the critical point, there is always the possibility of increasing taxes. Moreover, the taxable object of income tax has universality. Anyone with income that reaches a certain limit has the obligation to pay taxes, unlike other taxes that are levied only on specific objects, limited to a local area, and cannot be compared in terms of the amount of revenue. In wartime, funds are urgently needed, and the amounts are very large. Although public debt can sometimes be relied upon to cope with the situation, the raising of public debt depends on the people's absorption capacity and trust in the government, and ultimately, it must still be repaid through taxes. For this reason, every time a war occurs, the expenditure of huge war expenses is often dependent on income tax to be shared among the people. Therefore, the evolution of income tax is often driven by wartime finance.

Since World War I, social economies have reached a more highly developed stage. With the progress of economic conditions, the political landscape has formed two camps: the rise of socialism and the rise of fascism. Income tax, which was previously aimed at fiscal revenue, has been used by some countries as a tool to complete the social policies of their respective ideologies. Other countries, in addition to fiscal purposes, also use it to harmonize the distribution of wealth among various social classes to alleviate conflicts. The former includes the Soviet Union and Italy, while the latter is the consistent trend of most countries that implement income tax today. Let's briefly discuss the recent income tax systems of the Soviet Union and Italy to clarify the relationship between income tax and social policy. The relationship between income tax and social policy.

Since the implementation of the New Economic Policy and the restoration of monetary taxes, income tax has been adopted in the Soviet Union. However, the adoption of income tax was initially not for fiscal revenue but to achieve the goal of socialism. According to the provisions of its tax law, it can be described as follows:

(1) Strict classification of taxable classes: The Soviet Union attaches great importance to the status and tasks of various classes in society. Therefore, it divides income into six types and stipulates different tax rates based on their social status.

(2) Heavy taxation on private and private enterprise income and light taxation on collective and state enterprise income: The Soviet Union advocates the nationalization of industries and actively promotes non-capitalist collective enterprises and state-owned enterprises, while advocating the abolition of private individuals and private enterprises. Therefore, it levies heavy taxes on them to allow for their natural elimination.

(3) For agriculture, it is also divided into four classes: collective farms, non-collectivized property of collective farms, individually operated farms, and wealthy peasants. The tax rates are the lightest for collective farms, followed by non-collectivized property of collective farms, then individually operated farms, and extremely harsh progressive taxes are levied on wealthy peasants. The Soviet Union advocates collective operation of agriculture and nationalization of farmland. Privately owned land operated independently is not allowed to exist, so heavy taxation on wealthy peasants is also intended to allow for their natural elimination.

(4) Widespread adoption of progressive tax rates: High progressive taxes are adopted for private income to limit the activities of private capital.

The social policy of the Soviet Union originally aimed at nationalizing all means of production as its highest goal. Therefore, its income tax system serves as a tool to restrict the activities of private capital and privately owned land, thereby achieving the goal of all private systems being naturally eliminated. Standing on the other side of socialist countries is fascist Italy. The social policy of Italy takes the protection of private capital as its principle, which is the so-called "principle of productivism." Therefore, its income tax system is also in the opposite position to that of the Soviet Union, but its role as a means of completing social policy is the same. Let's briefly discuss the relationship between the Italian income tax system and social policy for reference.

(1) After the establishment of the fascist government, various indirect taxes were successively increased, while in terms of income tax, the tax rates for movable property income tax, inheritance tax, and supplementary income tax were reduced. At the same time, agricultural income and labor income were also included in the scope of movable property income tax and levied. Although the agricultural income of semi-self-cultivating farmers and tenant farmers is the same as the labor income of workers and other movable property income, this violates the principle of fairness. However, to achieve the goal of protecting private capital, this point is disregarded.

The income tax in Italy is divided into two types: movable property income tax and supplementary income tax. The tax rate for movable property income tax adopts a proportional system, and the tax rate for supplementary income tax adopts a very slight progressive system. Therefore, the burden on high-income earners is not significantly different from that of low-income earners, which is intended to favor high-income earners to promote the development of private capital.

(2) Levying taxes on capitalists directly reduces their capital and harms their power to operate. Therefore, Italy strives to reduce the tax rate for income tax. On the one hand, it expands the scope of taxation as much as possible, so that the general working class and low-income earners are also subject to taxation, which runs counter to the general principle of "heavy taxation on high income and light taxation on low income" in various countries. However, capitalists receive preferential treatment with light tax rates, which helps their ability to operate. The principle of productivism seeks to avoid anything that hinders the increase of private wealth.

The Italian income tax system has been briefly described above. Contrasting it with the income tax system of the Soviet Union is truly interesting. As the progress of world politics tends to two opposite extremes, the income tax system naturally also diverges and evolves. Considering the nature of income tax in relation to social policy, it is more suitable for socialist Soviet Union than for fascist Italy.

Comparison of Personal Income Tax in China, the Philippines, and the United States 194

— Xie Juceng

The Shanghai English-language Da Mei Evening News recently commissioned its legal counsel to compare the personal income portion of China's income tax with the current tax rates in the United States and the Philippines, presenting the comparison in a chart with explanations. This is very detailed, and this article is based on the data from that newspaper. However, the original manuscript mistakenly stated that China's personal salary income starts to be taxed from 40 yuan, with the initial 30 yuan being the tax-exempt amount, which is slightly inconsistent with the facts. This is specifically corrected, along with the calculated figures. Translator's note

Why compare the tax rates of the United States with the tax rates in China's Provisional Income Tax Regulations? Because the income tax laws of other countries are intricate and difficult to compare. Only the United States' is relatively simple, and using it to compare with the extremely simple Chinese tax rates will avoid a mismatch. Secondly, the income tax law of the United States has been implemented for many years. There have been no major modification requests for the principles it establishes to date. Moreover, the Philippines uses American law as a blueprint and implements it in the Far East with great success. The standard of living in the Philippines is somewhat similar to that of China, so the Philippine law is used as a companion. In fact, the Philippine income tax law is no different from the United States in terms of basic principles, but the numbers are much lower than those of the United States. By comparing the tax rates of personal income tax in China, the Philippines, and the United States, we can discover many obvious differences. Now, let's briefly explain them.

(1) China distinguishes between personal salary income and securities deposit interest income, which does not exist in the United States and the Philippines. According to China's Provisional Regulations, personal service income is taxed starting from 30 yuan per month, gradually exceeding and progressing until 2% is levied on those earning 1,100 yuan per month. As for securities deposit interest income, regardless of the amount of income, 0.5% is levied uniformly. Now, if a person's monthly salary income is between 400 yuan and 500 yuan, the tax rate is 0.5%. For those between 500 yuan and 600 yuan, it is 0.6%. In fact, only 0.4% is levied on the initial 400 yuan, so the actual tax levied is less than 0.5% when the total income does not reach 700 yuan. However, when it exceeds 700 yuan, the tax levied is much heavier than that of securities deposit interest income. Because from 700 yuan onwards, the tax rate gradually increases. Assuming a person's monthly income reaches 1,200 yuan, the amount they are taxed is more than double that of a person who enjoys the same amount of securities deposit interest income.

(2) The United States' income tax system shows sympathy for those who live on salaries and wages. Not only is the tax rate very low, but those whose income just reaches the taxation standard are given a 10% discount.

(3) China's tax system has a rapid progression of tax rates for moderate and lower incomes, while the tax rates for those with huge monthly salaries progress more slowly. The United States and the Philippines treat everyone equally, regardless of their income level.

(4) China's tax system does not differentiate based on the taxpayer's family situation or the number of dependents they support. Taxpayers with family burdens must also follow the regulation of starting taxation from 30 yuan. As for the United States, the standard tax-exempt amount for monthly service income is equivalent to 302.50 yuan in Chinese currency. The tax-exempt amount for monthly non-service income is equivalent to 275 yuan in Chinese currency. If this person is married, the tax-exempt amount is increased to 755 yuan or 587.50 yuan. Once they have children, the tax-exempt amount is further increased by 110 yuan for each additional child or dependent relative. The average size of Chinese families has always been larger than the average size of American families, and in Chinese law, there are even crimes such as abandonment for failing to support helpless family members. However, the tax system has not paid attention to this point.

(5) China's tax system stipulates that personal monthly income is taxed starting from 30 yuan, so most shop clerks, secretaries, drivers, and machinists are included in the tax list. In the United States, the income of such people is far less than the prescribed tax-exempt amount, so they can be exempt from income tax.

(6) China stipulates that personal income tax must be paid monthly, twelve times a year, and the cost of collection seems to be larger than that of the United States and the Philippines, which collect once a year. The tax paid by low-level salary income taxpayers may only be enough to cover the collection costs of income tax personnel. If a person's monthly salary is 30 yuan and the tax paid is 5 cents, even if the employer withholds it on their behalf, the cost of recording and tabulating this account is probably equal to this tax amount. For those who do not have employers to withhold the tax, it is necessary to send personnel to collect it, which is too uneconomical.

When the United States started implementing income tax, the tax rate was lower than the one listed in the table in this article. It was gradually increased later, aiming to prevent the taxpayer's budget from being suddenly affected. However, although the US tax rate has been increased several times, it is still lower than China's initial tax rate, except for those with huge monthly salaries exceeding 15,600 yuan. Because according to the Chinese tax rate, if a person earns 1,000 yuan per month, the annual tax paid is equal to one month's salary. If they earn 1,100 yuan per month, their annual tax expenditure is simply more than one month's salary. In the United States, if this person's monthly income is less than 6,200 yuan in Chinese currency, the annual tax amount will definitely not reach one month's salary. In other words, taxpayers earning 1,000 yuan per month in China are treated the same as taxpayers earning 6,200 yuan per month in the United States. Those earning 6,200 yuan have about 500 yuan deducted each month, leaving 5,700 yuan. Although the standard of living in the United States is higher, it doesn't matter much, but for those earning 1,000 yuan, deducting 75 yuan will have some impact.

Comparison Table of Personal Salary Income Tax Amounts in China, the Philippines, and the United States

Note: The above tax amounts for the Philippines and the United States refer to taxpayers with a wife and one child. Adjustments are made for families with more or fewer members.

Calculation Table of Personal Salary Income Tax in China, the Philippines, and the United States

China: 1,200 yuan per month, 14,400 yuan per year; China tax amount: 1,363.20 yuan; 1,363.20 yuan divided by 14,400 yuan equals 9.46% (China tax rate)

United States tax amount: 131.76 yuan; 131.76 yuan divided by 14,400 yuan equals 9.2% (United States tax rate)

Philippines tax amount: 12.96 yuan; 12.96 yuan divided by 14,400 yuan equals 7% (Philippines tax rate)

Securities - A Review of the Bond Market Situation for the Past Week 195

Last week, from November 16th to 21st, at the Chinese Securities Exchange, market fluctuations were entirely dictated by the waxing and waning of the Suiyuan War. Various groups had been overly bullish, resulting in overcrowded positions. Consequently, encountering the Suiyuan War led to a flurry of selling, causing prices to fall. However, with the Suiyuan War intensifying, the bond market's volatility is just beginning. Last week's events: On Monday, the Suiyuan War was poised to expand, worsening the situation, and bullish investors began to sell, with small declines ranging from 6 to 6.25%. On Tuesday, the front-line situation became increasingly tense, and selling surged, with further small declines ranging from 6.25 to 6.75%. On Wednesday, President Chiang's visit to Taiyuan heightened the atmosphere, and the war intensified, causing another decline of 0.25 to 6.75%. On Thursday, news of a victory at the front lines boosted morale, and President Chiang returned to Luoyang. Market prices suddenly turned upward, trending higher throughout the day, with a sudden increase of 0.3125 to 6.8125%. On Friday, the front-line situation showed signs of expansion, the background was clear, and the market relaxed, with a small decline of 0.125 to 6.625%. On Saturday, retail investors engaged in some short-covering, causing a slight rebound of 0.03125 to 6.25%. As a result, market prices were slightly lower than the previous week, ranging from 6.0625% to 6.1875%, except for the Gold Bond, which rose by 1 yuan. Cotton Yarn - US Cotton Futures Rebound Strongly, Influenced by Italy's Removal of Foreign Exchange Restrictions 196

Yesterday, US cotton opened with gains ranging from 0.0625 pound to a decline of 0.25 pound for various months. December futures saw some liquidation and swaps, with few sellers. Traders and shorts bought in, and all short-selling positions were absorbed. Although the ginning volume was high, the market trend remained firm. Spot prices were able to maintain. Within the week, cloth sales exceeded half of the production volume. Before the close, it was reported that Italy had removed restrictions on foreign exchange, causing market prices to rise. Spot prices rose by 0.25 pound, and futures rose by 0.25 to 1.1875 pound. British cotton spot prices fell by 0.01875 pound, and futures rose by 0.0625 pound. Indian cotton rose due to high purchase orders for Oomra cotton and reports of heavy rains in central regions. However, it slightly retreated due to long liquidation.
